Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Qada for Child Reaching Puberty and Disbeliever Accepting Islam During Ramadan
Ruling on qada for those who become eligible during Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a child reaching puberty or a disbeliever accepting Islam during Ramadan, and identify the three proofs supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
Fasts missed before eligibility require no qada.

When does fasting become obligatory for a child who becomes mature during the day, or a disbeliever who accepts Islam? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: only fasts missed after the moment of eligibility require qada. You will learn the proofs from rational argument, the Quran, and the Hadith of the Thaqif delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Exception
Read the opening sentences: 'Upon them is qada except for the last two.' Identify the two excepted categories (child and new Muslim) and note that qada is required for others but not for these two regarding fasts before their eligibility.
The 'last two' refer to the child and the new Muslim.
2
Understand the Rationale (Eligibility at Dawn)
The text explains that the fast of a given day is not fard if the person was not a Muslim or not mature at dawn (subh sadiq). Grasp the principle: obligation attaches at dawn; eligibility at that moment determines whether the day's fast must be made up.
If eligibility occurs after dawn, that day's fast is not owed.
3
Analyze the Quranic Proof
The verse (2:183) addresses 'those who believe'. Discuss how this restricts the obligation to believers, thus a disbeliever is not addressed and prior fasts are not required.
The dalal is zanni but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Examine the Hadith Proof
The hadith from Bayhaqi reports that the Prophet ﷺ ordered the new Muslims to fast only the remaining days and did not command qada for past days. Recognise this as a specific evidence for the exception.
This hadith overrides any general implication that all missed fasts must be made up.
5
Apply the Ruling to Practical Cases
Work through the examples: a disbeliever becomes Muslim at 11 AM on the 5th; a child reaches puberty at the same time. Conclude that they owe no qada for the 5th or any earlier day; they must fast from the next day onward.
This matches the hadith: they fast what remains of the month.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
الفجر وعلى صبي بلغ وكافر اسلم (۱۰۹۷) وعليهم القضاء الا الاخيرين.
يومها قال : لا يأكلان حتى يمسيان - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المسافر يقدم في بعض النهار والحائض تظهر في بعضه ، ج رابع ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۷۳۸۴ مصنف ابن ابی شیبیۃ ، باب في المرأة تحیض في رمضان أول النهار، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۰ نمبر ۹۳۴۰) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ حائضہ اور مسافر باقی دن کھانے سے رکے رہیں۔
ترجمه : (۱۰۹۷) اور اخیر کے دو کے علاوہ (بچہ اور نو مسلم ) سب پر قضا ہے۔
تشریح : مثلا کا فر۵ ارمضان میں گیارہ بجے سے پہلے مسلمان ہوا، یا بچہ گیارہ بجے سے پہلے بالغ ہوا تو ان دونوں پر ۱۵ رمضان کی قضا نہیں اور نہ اس سے پہلے کے روزے کی قضا ہے، کیونکہ اس سے پہلے یہ روزے کے اہل نہیں تھے ، ہاں ۱۵ کے بعد جتنے روزے ہیں وہ فرض ہوں گے یا اس وقت ادا کرے یا بعد میں قضا کرے۔ اور ان دو کے علاوہ جتنے لوگ ہیں ان پر پہلے کے روزے بھی فرض ہیں اور جس دن روزہ رکھنے کے اہل ہوئے اس دن کے روزہ بھی واجب ہے، کیونکہ یہ لوگ پہلے سے روزہ واجب ہونے
کے اہل چلے آرہے ہیں صرف خارجی مجبوری کی وجہ سے ابھی روزہ نہیں رکھ سک رہے ہیں اس لئے بعد میں قضا کرے۔ وجه : (۱) اور ۵ رمضان کا روزہ اس لئے فرض نہیں ہو گا کہ اس کی صبح صادق کے وقت کا فرمسلمان نہیں تھا اور بچہ بالغ نہیں تھا، اور گویا کہ یہ دن اول وقت میں روزہ فرض ہونے کے اہل نہیں تھے۔ (۲) کافر روزہ رکھنے کا اہل نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے (ا)يا ايها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم الصيام كما كتب على الذين من قبلكم لعلكم تتقون ( آیت۱۸۳،سورة البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مومن پر روزہ فرض ہے اس لئے کافر پر فرض نہیں ہوگا ۔ (۳) اسلام لانے سے پہلے کا روزہ قضا کرنا واجب نہیں اور بعد کی قضا کرنا واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سفيان بن عطية بن ربيعة الثقفي قال قدم وفدنا
صلى الله
من ثقيف على النبي لعل الله فضرب لهم قبة و اسلموا في النصف من رمضان فامرهم رسول الله الله فصاموا منه ما استقبلوا منه و لم يامرهم بقضاء ما فاتهم - ( سنن بیہقی ، باب الرجل يسلم في خلال شهر رمضان، ج رابع ،
ص ۴۴۸، نمبر ۸۳۰۸)
Chapter: At dawn, and concerning a child who reaches puberty and a disbeliever who accepts Islam (1097): Upon them is qada except for the last two. They said: They should not eat until evening. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab al-Musafir Yaqdimu fi Ba'd al-Nahar..., vol. 4, p. 132, no. 7384; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab al-Mar'ah Tahidu fi Ramadan Awwal al-Nahar, vol. 2, p. 1310, no. 9340) In this report, it is also that the menstruating woman and traveler should refrain from eating for the rest of the day. Translation: (1097) And except for the last two (the child and the new Muslim), qada is upon everyone. Explanation: For example, if a disbeliever becomes Muslim before 11 o'clock on the 5th of Ramadan, or a child reaches puberty before 11 o'clock, then qada is not required from them for the 5th of Ramadan, nor for fasts before that, because before that they were not qualified for fasting. Yes, for fasts after the 5th, they are fard; they should either perform them on time or make them up later. As for others besides these two, the previous fasts are also fard upon them, and the fast of the day they became eligible is also wajib, because these people were already eligible for the obligation of fasting; only an external compulsion prevents them from fasting now, so they should make it up later. Reason: (1) The fast of the 5th of Ramadan is not fard because at the time of dawn (subh sadiq), he was not a Muslim or the child was not mature, so they were not eligible for the obligation of fasting at the beginning of the day. (2) A disbeliever is not qualified to fast; the proof is this verse: “O you who have believed, decreed upon you is fasting as it was decreed upon those before you that you may become righteous” (Surah al-Baqarah 2:183). This verse indicates that fasting is fard upon believers, so it is not fard upon a disbeliever. (3) Qada of fasts before embracing Islam is not wajib, but qada of fasts after is wajib. The proof is this hadith: From Sufyan ibn 'Atiyyah ibn Rabi'ah al-Thaqafi who said: Our delegation from Thaqif came to the Prophet ﷺ and he set up a dome for them, and they embraced Islam in the middle of Ramadan. Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ordered them to fast what remained of the month, and did not order them to make up what they had missed. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Rajul Yusalimu fi Khilal Shahr Ramadan, vol. 4, p. 448, no. 8308)
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning qada (making up missed fasts) for a child who reaches puberty during Ramadan or a disbeliever who accepts Islam during Ramadan. The author states that except for these two (the child and the new Muslim), everyone else is required to make up missed fasts. The explanation clarifies that if a disbeliever becomes Muslim or a child reaches puberty before dawn, they must fast that day and make up any subsequent missed fasts. However, they are not required to make up fasts from before their eligibility. The proofs provided are: (1) a rational argument that they were not eligible at the time of obligation; (2) the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah which addresses believers, indicating that fasting is not obligated upon disbelievers; and (3) a hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi where the Prophet ﷺ ordered new Muslims to fast only the remaining days of Ramadan, without commanding them to make up the past days. This shows that prior fasts are not wajib to make up.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act (fast) after its time.
صبي بلغ (sabi balagha): A child who has reached puberty (maturity).
كافر اسلم (kafir aslama): A disbeliever who embraces Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A child reaches puberty at 10 AM on Ramadan 5. According to the Hanafi school, which statement is correct?
A) He must make up the fast of that day and all previous days.
B) He must make up the fast of that day only.
C) He must fast from the next day and make up any subsequent days if missed, but not the previous days or that day.
D) He is not required to fast at all because he was not mature at the start of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, fasting obligations are linked to eligibility at dawn; a new Muslim or newly mature child only owes fasts from the time of their eligibility.

Seven Disliked Actions for a Fasting Person
List of seven disliked actions for a fasting person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven disliked actions for a fasting person and distinguish between makruh and permissible actions when an excuse is present.

Core Idea
Seven actions are disliked for the fasting person, but the fast remains valid as long as nothing reaches the throat.

This lesson presents the seven actions considered makruh (disliked) for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school. The list includes tasting, chewing, kissing, and cupping, among others. Understanding these rulings helps the fasting person avoid diminishing their reward while preserving the validity of their fast. Importantly, if a genuine need arises, these actions become permissible as long as nothing is swallowed.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the seven items
Commit the list to memory: (1) tasting without excuse, (2) chewing without excuse, (3) chewing 'ilk (gum), (4) kissing, (5) embracing if not secure, (6) swallowing gathered saliva, (7) actions causing weakness (e.g., phlebotomy, cupping).
Use mnemonic: T-C-K-K-E-S-P (Taste, Chew, Gum, Kiss, Embrace, Spit, Phlebotomy).
2
Identify the condition of 'without excuse'
Each action is only makruh when performed without a valid excuse. The text explicitly mentions 'without excuse' for tasting/chewing, implying the same for others.
An excuse could be a hot-tempered husband needing to taste food, or a mother needing to chew for her child.
3
Understand the exception: swallowing invalidates
Even with an excuse, if any substance reaches the throat, the fast is broken. The ruling applies only when no swallowing occurs.
The proof from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i states: 'There is no harm if a woman chews for her child while fasting, as long as it does not enter her throat.'
4
Distinguish makruh tanzih from tahrimi
These are likely makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) because the fast remains valid. If they were makruh tahrimi, they would be close to haram and require qada.
The fast is valid but reward diminished.

Source Text

...... اور علک (ایک قسم کا زرد گوند جو پستے کے درخت سے نکلتا ہے ) کا چبانا۔

تشریح : مجبوری ہو تو کسی چیز کا چکھنایا چبانا جائز ہے،مثلا شو ہر تند مزاج ہے تو سالن چکے یا بچے کو کھانا چبا کر دینے کی مجبوری ہو تو ماں چبا کر دے سکتی ہے، بشرطیکہ کہ حلق کے اندر نہ جائے ورنہ روزہ ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ اور یہ مجبوری نہیں ہے تو روزہ دار کے لئے اس کا

وجه : (۱) قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال لا بأس ان تمضغ المرأة لصبيها وهي صائمة مالم تدخل حلقها (مصنف ابن ابي شبيبة ، ۵۰ فی الصائمة تمضغ لصبيها ج ثانی ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۹۲۹۳ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب المرأة تمضغ لصبيها وهى صائمة و تذوق الشيء ، ج رابع ، ص ۱۵۹، نمبر ۷۵۴۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت پڑے تو عورت اپنے بچے کے لئے کھانا چبا

تشریح : ملک ایک تم کا گوند ہے جو دانت صاف کرنے کے لئے عورتیں چہاتی ہیں۔ اس لئے اگر صرف دانت صاف کرنے
Chapter: Concerning what is disliked for a fasting person, what is not disliked, and what is recommended. (Seven things are disliked for a fasting person) (1098) Tasting something and chewing it without an excuse. (1099) Chewing 'ilk (a type of gum). Summary: Regarding disliked, non-disliked, and recommended things for a fasting person. Seven things are disliked for a fasting person: [1] Tasting something without an excuse. [2] Chewing. [3] Chewing 'ilk (a yellow gum extracted from the pistachio tree). [4] Kissing. [5] Embracing one's wife, if not secure from desire. [6] Gathering saliva in the mouth and then swallowing it. [7] Anything that is thought to weaken the fasting person, such as phlebotomy and cupping. Translation: (1098) [1] Tasting something without an excuse. [2] Chewing. Explanation: If there is a necessity, tasting or chewing is permissible, for example, if the husband is hot-tempered, tasting the curry, or if there is a need to chew food for a child, the mother may chew and give, provided it does not reach the throat; otherwise the fast will break. If there is no necessity, then tasting or chewing is makruh for the fasting person. Reason: There is a saying of a Tabi'i: from Ibrahim who said: 'There is no harm if a woman chews for her child while fasting, as long as it does not enter her throat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 9293; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, no. 7541) From this report, it is understood that when necessary, a woman can chew food for her child, provided the food does not reach her throat. Translation: (1099) [3] Chewing 'ilk. Explanation: 'Ilk is a gum that women chew to clean their teeth. So if only for cleaning teeth...
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating seven things that are disliked (makruh) for a fasting person. The author lists: (1) tasting something without excuse, (2) chewing without excuse, (3) chewing 'ilk (a type of gum), (4) kissing, (5) embracing one's wife if not secure from desire, (6) gathering saliva in the mouth and swallowing it, and (7) anything that weakens the fasting person like phlebotomy and cupping. The explanation adds that if there is a genuine need, tasting or chewing is permissible as long as nothing reaches the throat. A proof from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i is cited allowing a woman to chew for her child when necessary. The passage ends with an incomplete explanation of 'ilk. The author emphasizes the distinction between excused and unexcused actions.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked in the Shari'ah; avoiding it brings reward, but doing it is not sinful.
علک ('ilk): A type of gum used for cleaning teeth.
مذاق (madhaq): Tasting food or drink without swallowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered makruh for a fasting person?
A) Using a miswak
B) Chewing gum ('ilk) without an excuse
C) Taking a shower
D) Applying kohl

Key Takeaway
Seven actions are disliked (makruh tanzih) for the fasting person, but none break the fast unless swallowing occurs; with a genuine excuse, they become permissible.

Kissing and Physical Contact During Fasting
Ruling on kissing and touching with hadith proofs and age-based distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing and mubasharah while fasting and identify the condition that determines whether it is makruh or permissible.

Core Idea
Kissing while fasting is makruh only if there is fear of desire leading to ejaculation or intercourse; otherwise it is permissible.

This lesson addresses a practical question: Is it permissible for a fasting person to kiss or embrace their spouse? The Hanafi school makes a nuanced distinction based on the risk of desire and loss of control. We will examine the ruling as stated in the classical texts, supported by two important hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act in question is kissing (qublah) and non-penetrative physical contact (mubasharah). The default ruling in the Hanafi school is not absolute prohibition but a conditional dislike (karahah).
Mubasharah here means touching without penetration, often over clothes.
2
Understand the condition that triggers karahah
The ruling depends on whether the person feels safe from ejaculation (inzal) or intercourse (jima). If there is fear, it is makruh; if safe, it is permissible.
This condition is subjective and varies with age and self-control.
3
Analyze the first hadith proof
The hadith from Aisha (ra) shows that the Prophet (saw) himself kissed while fasting. This establishes that the act itself is not prohibited.
The Prophet's high level of control (amlakukum li-arbihi) is highlighted.
4
Analyze the second hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Huraira tells of the Prophet permitting an old man but prohibiting a young man. This indicates that the ruling changes based on the risk of desire.
The distinction is between those who can control their desires and those who cannot.
5
Contrast with other schools
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers kissing and touching permissible for all without karahah, as long as no seminal emission occurs. The Hanafi position is more cautious.
This difference is due to varying weight given to the hadith of Aisha vs. the general principle of avoiding temptation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يكره للصائم
والقبلة والمباشرة ان لم يـامـن فيهما على نفسه الانزال او الجماع في ظاهر الرواية
ترجمه : (۱۱۰۰)[۴] بوسہ دینا۔ [۵] اور بیوی سے لپٹنا، اگر ان دونوں میں اپنی ذات پر انزال ہونے کا یا جماع کر ڈالنے سے امن نہ ہو تو مکروہ ہے۔ ظاہر روایت میں۔
تشریح : اگر اس بات کا خطرہ ہو کہ بیوی کو بوسہ دینے سے یا لپٹنے سے انزال ہو جائے گا، یا آگے جماع کر ڈالے گا تو بوسہ لینا اور لپٹنا مکروہ ہے، لیکن اگر اس کا خطرہ نہیں ہے، مثلا آدمی بوڑھا ہے تو بوسہ لینے ، یا لپٹ جانے کی گنجائش ہے۔
وجه: (ا) عن عائشة قالت كان النبى الله يقبل ويباشر و هو صائم و كان أملككم لاربه (بخارى شريف، باب المباشر للصائم ، ص ۳۰۹، نمبر ۱۹۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے روزے کی حالت میں بوسہ لیا ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رجلا سال النبي الله عن المباشرة للصائم فرخص له واتاه آخر فنهاه فاذا الذي رخص له شيخ والذى نهاه شاب ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کراہیة للشاب ص ۳۳۱ نمبر ۷ ۲۳۸) حدیث میں جو ان کو روکنے کی وجہ یہی تھی کہ اس کو نفس پر قابو نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مکر وہ ہوگا۔
لغت: مردعورت کی شرمگاہ میں داخل نہ کرے صرف اوپر اوپر سے ملائے تو اس کو مباشرت فاحشہ کہتے ہیں ۔ قبل: بوسہ لینا۔
Chapter: What is disliked for the fasting person. And kissing and direct contact, if one does not feel safe in them from ejaculation or intercourse, in the apparent narration. Translation: (1100) [4] Kissing. [5] And embracing the wife; if in these two there is fear of ejaculation or intercourse, it is disliked. In the apparent narration. Explanation: If there is danger that from kissing or embracing the wife ejaculation will occur, or later intercourse, then kissing and embracing are disliked. But if there is no such danger, e.g., the man is old, then there is leeway for kissing or embracing. Evidence: (1) From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss and touch while fasting, and he was the most controlling of his desires. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of direct contact for the fasting person, p. 309, no. 1927). This hadith shows that the Prophet kissed while fasting. (2) In a hadith: From Abu Huraira that a man asked the Prophet about direct contact while fasting, and he permitted him; then another came and he prohibited him; the one permitted was an old man and the one prohibited was a young man. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter of dislike for the young, p. 331, no. 7238). The reason for prohibiting the young was that he could not control his desires. Therefore it is disliked. Lexicon: If a man does not insert into the private part but merely touches over the clothes, this is called immodest direct contact. Qubla: kissing.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the ruling on kissing and physical contact (mubasharah) for a fasting person. The author states that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) of the Hanafi school, these actions are makruh (disliked) if one fears that they may lead to ejaculation (inzal) or intercourse (jima'). The word 'mubasharah' here means non-penetrative physical contact between husband and wife. The key condition is the fear of losing control. If the individual is confident of self-control, e.g., an elderly person, the action is not makruh. The author supports this with two hadith: first, from Aisha that the Prophet himself kissed while fasting, showing permissibility; second, from Abu Huraira that the Prophet permitted an old man but prohibited a young man, indicating that the ruling hinges on the risk of arousal. Thus, the ruling is clear: kissing and touching are not inherently prohibited but become makruh when there is genuine fear of invalidating the fast.

Key Terms
قبلة (qublah): Kissing between spouses
مباشرة (mubāsharah): Direct physical contact between spouses without penetration
انزال (inzāl): Ejaculation of semen

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is correct about kissing during fasting?
A) It is always haram.
B) It is makruh only if one fears it may lead to ejaculation or intercourse.
C) It is always permissible for anyone.
D) It is only permissible for old people.

Key Takeaway
Kissing and touching while fasting are makruh only when there is a genuine fear of desire leading to a violation of the fast; otherwise, they remain permissible.

Ruling on Collecting and Swallowing Saliva While Fasting
Ruling on intentionally collecting and swallowing saliva while fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on collecting and swallowing saliva during fasting and identify the evidence from the Salaf that supports it.

Core Idea
Swallowing intentionally collected saliva is disliked (makruh) but does not break the fast, as it is internal.

This lesson addresses a common question: may a fasting person collect saliva in the mouth and deliberately swallow it? The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between internal and external substances. Understanding this ruling helps avoid unnecessary qada' while maintaining the proper reverence for fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is intentionally collecting saliva in the mouth and swallowing it. The ruling: the fast is valid (not broken), but the act is makruh (disliked).
The ruling applies only when done intentionally; normal swallowing of saliva is not makruh.
2
Examine the evidence from the Salaf
The passage cites three athar: (1) Ibn Umar's practice of not swallowing saliva after using miswak, (2) Ibrahim al-Nakha'i's permission to chew gum provided nothing enters the throat, (3) Umm Habiba's disapproval of chewing gum for the fasting person.
These reports indicate that while the fast is not broken, avoiding such acts is recommended.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Only external substances that reach the stomach break the fast. Saliva originates from inside the body, so swallowing it does not nullify fasting.
This principle also applies to chewing gum: as long as no particles are swallowed, the fast remains valid.
4
Apply to analogous cases
The same principle applies to any substance that originates from within the body (e.g., blood from gums) – swallowing it does not break the fast unless it is external matter.
Chewing gum without swallowing is analogous to saliva if no particles enter the throat.
5
Note the ethical dimension
The disliked nature (karahah) stems from the act resembling eating or drinking and being unnecessary. A fasting person should avoid such acts to maintain the spirit of abstinence.
This ruling encourages self-restraint beyond the minimum requirements.

لغت : مفغ : چبانا ۔ العلک : چبانے کا گوند۔
ترجمه : (۱۱۰۱) [1] اور منھ میں تھوک کو جمع کرنا پھر اسے نگل لینا۔
تشریح : منہ میں تھوک جمع کرے اور اس کو نگل جائے تو اس سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا، کیونکہ اندر کی چیز ہے ،لیکن ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے وجه : و قال ابن عمر يستاك اول النهار و آخره و لا يبلع ريقه - (بخاری شریف، باب انفنسال الصائم، ص ۱۳۱۰، نمبر ۱۹۳۰)
(1101) And collecting saliva in the mouth then swallowing it. For (chewing gum) if one chews and spits it out and no particle goes down the throat, the fast is not broken, because nothing entered the stomach. But doing so is makruh. Evidence: (1) There is an athar from Ibrahim that he permitted chewing gum for the fasting person as long as nothing enters his throat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 31, p. 297, no. 9179) This athar shows that chewing gum does not break the fast provided nothing enters the throat. (2) Chewing without need is makruh. Its proof is the saying of a tabi'i: from Umm Habiba, wife of the Prophet (peace be upon her), that she disliked chewing gum for the fasting person. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 32, p. 298, no. 9186; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, 4, p. 447, no. 8306) This athar states that chewing gum is makruh for the fasting person. Principle: The ruling is that if gum reaches the stomach, the fast breaks; otherwise not. Lexicon: Madgh: chewing; al-‘ilk: chewing gum. Translation: (1101) [1] And collecting saliva in the mouth then swallowing it. Explanation: If one collects saliva in the mouth and swallows it, the fast is not broken, because it is an internal substance. But doing so is makruh. Evidence: And Ibn Umar said: He uses the miswak at the beginning and end of the day and does not swallow his saliva. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of the fasting person's saliva, p. 1310, no. 1930).
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on intentionally collecting saliva in the mouth and then swallowing it during fasting. The author rules that doing so does not break the fast because saliva is an internal bodily fluid, and only external substances entering the stomach nullify the fast. However, it is considered makruh (disliked) because it resembles eating or drinking unnecessarily. The text also includes a discussion on chewing gum ('ilk) as an analogy: chewing gum is permissible as long as no particles are swallowed, but it is makruh without necessity. The evidence comes from athar (sayings of the Salaf): Ibrahim al-Nakha'i permitted chewing gum if nothing enters the throat, and Umm Habiba disliked it. Additionally, the statement of Ibn Umar that he does not swallow his saliva after using the miswak supports the recommendation to avoid swallowing saliva unnecessarily. The underlying principle is that the fast is only broken by something reaching the stomach; saliva originates from inside, so swallowing it does not break the fast.

Key Terms
ريق (rīq): Saliva or spittle
ابتلاع (ibtilā‘): The act of swallowing
علک (‘ilk): Chewing gum or any masticatory substance

A) It breaks the fast and requires qada'
B) It does not break the fast and is not makruh
C) It does not break the fast but is makruh
D) It breaks the fast and requires kaffarah

Key Takeaway
Collecting and swallowing saliva during fasting is permissible (fast valid) but disliked (makruh) because it is unnecessary and resembles eating.

Cupping and Phlebotomy During Fasting: Ruling and Hadith Reconciliation
Ruling on actions that weaken the fasting person like cupping and phlebotomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that cupping does not break the fast but is makruh tanzih, and reconcile the apparent contradictory hadith.

Core Idea
Cupping does not break the fast but is makruh because it causes weakness — the fast is valid but reward is diminished.

This lesson explores the ruling on actions that weaken the fasting person, such as cupping and bloodletting. You may have heard conflicting hadith about whether cupping breaks the fast. The Hanafi school harmonizes them in a way that preserves the fast's validity while discouraging acts that jeopardize it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the ruling
Recognize that cupping (hijamah) and phlebotomy (fasd) are actions that cause weakness. The author states they are makruh.
Makruh here means makruh tanzih (disliked, not prohibited).
2
Examine the primary hadith
Note the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Ibn Abbas that clearly state cupping does not break the fast.
These hadith establish the basic ruling that the fast remains valid.
3
Examine the contradictory hadith
Look at the hadith of Thawban: 'The cupper and the one cupped have broken the fast.' This seems to contradict the first set.
The verb 'afṭara' literally means 'broke the fast'.
4
Understand the Hanafi reconciliation
The Hanafi scholars interpret 'afṭara' figuratively to mean 'the fast is brought close to breaking' or 'the reward is diminished due to weakness.' This harmonizes both sets of hadith.
This is a typical Hanafi method of jam' (reconciliation) rather than tarjih (preference).
5
Derive the final hukm
The reconciled ruling: cupping does not nullify the fast, but it is makruh tanzih because it causes weakness that may lead to breaking the fast.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

تشریح : جس چیز سے روزہ رکھنے میں کمزوری آجائے وہ کام کرنا مکروہ ہے، مثلا پچھنا لگوانے سے یا فصد کھلوانے سے آدمی کو کمزوری ہو جاتی ہے، اور ممکن ہے کہ روزہ توڑ دے اس لئے یہ کام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔

وجه : (۱) پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے خون نکلتا ہے بدن میں داخل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا ، حدیث یہ گزری ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال قال رسول الله الله : ثلاث لا يفطرن الصائم : الحجامة و القىء و الاحتلام ( ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصائم يزرعہ القی ص ۱۵۲ نمبر ۷۱۹ ابوداؤد شریف، فی الصائم محتلم نھا رافی شهر رمضان ص ۳۳۰ نمبر ۲۳۷۶ / بخاری شریف، باب الحجامة والقيمي للصائم، نمبر ۱۹۳۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال : احتجم النبى الله و هو صائم ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الحجامة والقیی للصائم، نمبر ۱۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے روزے کی حالت میں پچھنا لگوایا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا ۔ (۳) لیکن دوسری حدیث ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹے جائے گا، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ثـوبـان عـن النبي الله قال : أفطر الحاجم و المحجوم (ابوداؤد شریف فی الصائم محکم نھارانی شھر رمضان ص۳۳۰ نمبر ۲۳۶۷ متر مندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی کراھیة الحجامة للصائم ،ص۱۹۴، نمبر ۷۷۴ بخاری شریف ، باب الحجامة والقی للصائم ،نمبر (۱۹۳۸) یعنی روزہ ٹوٹنے کے قریب ہو گیا، اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔
لغت : الفصد : پچھلے زمانے میں رگ کاٹ کر مردہ خود نکالتے تھے اس کو فصد کہتے ہیں۔ الحجامہ : گردن کے اندرسوراخ کر کے منہ سے خون چوستے اور اس کو نکالتے تھے اس کو حجامت کہتے ہیں۔
(1102) And everything that is thought to weaken him, like phlebotomy and cupping. Chapter: What is disliked for the fasting person. Translation: (1102) [7] And everything that is thought to weaken him, like phlebotomy and cupping. Explanation: Any action that causes weakness during fasting is makruh, e.g., cupping or phlebotomy, because it may cause one to break the fast. Therefore it is makruh. Evidence: (1) A hadith has already passed that cupping does not break the fast because blood exits and does not enter the body. The hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Messenger of Allah said: Three things do not break the fast of the fasting person: cupping, vomiting, and nocturnal emission. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on cupping, p. 152, no. 719; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on fasting, p. 330, no. 2376; Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on cupping, no. 1938). This hadith shows that cupping does not break the fast. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet had cupping done while fasting. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on cupping and vomiting, no. 1939). This hadith shows that the Prophet had cupping while fasting, so it does not break the fast. (3) But there is another hadith that cupping breaks the fast: From Thawban from the Prophet: The cupper and the one cupped have broken the fast. (Sunan Abi Dawud, p. 330, no. 2367; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on dislike of cupping for the fasting, p. 194, no. 774; Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on cupping, no. 1938). This means the fast is close to being broken, therefore it is makruh. Lexicon: al-Fasd: In earlier times, cutting a vein to extract blood; al-Hijamah: Making a hole in the neck and sucking blood out with the mouth.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage addresses actions that weaken the fasting person, specifically phlebotomy (fasd) and cupping (hijamah). The author rules that although these actions do not break the fast (since blood exits the body and no substance enters), they are nevertheless makruh (disliked) because they cause weakness that may lead to breaking the fast. This ruling is derived from reconciling apparently contradictory hadith. The first set of hadith (from Abu Sa'id and Ibn Abbas) clearly state that cupping does not break the fast. However, a hadith from Thawban says that the cupper and the one cupped have 'afṭara' (broke the fast). The Hanafi interpretation is that the latter hadith means the fast is brought close to breaking (i.e., the action is makruh, not that it actually nullifies the fast). This is a typical Hanafi approach to resolving conflict between hadith by harmonizing them: one set establishes the basic ruling (no breaking), the other establishes the karahah. Thus, the final ruling is that cupping and similar weakening actions are makruh tanzih (disliked but not prohibited).

Key Terms
فصد (faṣd): Phlebotomy; opening a vein to draw blood
حجامة (ḥijāmah): Cupping; making incisions and sucking out blood
أفطر (afṭara): Literally 'broke the fast'; here interpreted as 'brought close to breaking' or 'invalidated in terms of reward'

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it causes weakness and may lead to breaking the fast
C) Because it is a forbidden medical practice
D) Because it involves extracting blood

Key Takeaway
Cupping does not invalidate the fast but is makruh tanzih because it causes weakness; the Hanafi reconciliation of hadith shows the subtlety of fiqh istinbat.

Cupping and Phlebotomy While Fasting: Disliked but Not Invalidating
Ruling and proof for cupping/phlebotomy being disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cupping (hijama) and phlebotomy (fasd) during fasting, cite the conflicting hadith, and explain why the ruling is makruh tanzih rather than haram or mubah.

Core Idea
Cupping does not break the fast but is disliked because it weakens the body.

Fasting requires avoiding not only nullifiers but also actions that compromise the spirit or strength of the fast. Among such actions are cupping and phlebotomy, which were common medical practices in the prophetic era and remain relevant today. In this passage, the author explains that while these actions do not invalidate the fast, they are disliked (makruh) because they weaken the fasting person, potentially leading to breaking the fast. He then reconciles apparent contradictory hadith to arrive at this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on cupping (hijama) and phlebotomy (fasd) during fasting. The hukm is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid but not prohibited.
2
Examine the proofs: hadith affirming permissibility
Two hadith indicate cupping does not break the fast: the Prophet's statement that three things do not break the fast (including cupping) and the Prophet himself being cupped while fasting. These show the act is not a nullifier.
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Ibn Abbas.
3
Examine the opposing proof: hadith suggesting invalidation
A third hadith from Thawban states 'The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast.' This seems to contradict the first two.
The author reconciles by interpreting 'afṭara' as 'nearly broke' or implying karahah, not actual nullification.
4
Apply the Hanafi reconciliation method
The Hanafi school gives weight to the more explicit and numerous proofs. The third hadith is interpreted as indicating that the fast is nearly broken, hence disliked, but not actually invalidated.
This reconciliation is based on the principle of jam' (harmonization) rather than tarjih (preference).
5
State the final mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling: cupping and phlebotomy are permissible but makruh tanzihan during fasting. They do not require qada or kaffarah.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and the majority of the Hanafi school.

فصل فيما يكره للصائم
(1102) وما ظنّ انه يضعّفه كالفصد والحجامة .
ترجمه : (1102) [۷] اور ہر اس چیز کے گمان سے جو اسے کمزور کر دیں، جیسے فصد اور حجامت ۔ تشریح : جس چیز سے روزہ رکھنے میں کمزوری آجائے وہ کام کرنا مکروہ ہے، مثلا پچھنا لگوانے سے یا فصد کھلوانے سے آدمی کو کمزوری ہو جاتی ہے، اور ممکن ہے کہ روزہ توڑ دے اس لئے یہ کام کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
وجه : (۱) پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے خون نکلتا ہے بدن میں داخل نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹے گا ، حدیث یہ گزری ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال قال رسول الله الله : ثلاث لا يفطرن الصائم : الحجامة و القىء و الاحتلام (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصائم يزرعہ القی ص ۱۵۲ نمبر ۷۱۹ ابوداؤد شریف، فی الصائم محتلم نھا رافی شهر رمضان ص ۳۳۰ نمبر ۲۳۷۶ / بخاری شریف، باب الحجامة والقيمي للصائم، نمبر ۱۹۳۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال : احتجم النبى الله و هو صائم ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الحجامة والقیی للصائم، نمبر ۱۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے روزے کی حالت میں پچھنا لگوایا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا ۔ (۳) لیکن دوسری حدیث ہے کہ پچھنا لگوانے سے روزہ ٹوٹے جائے گا، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ثـوبـان عـن النبي الله قال : أفطر الحاجم و المحجوم (ابوداؤد شریف فی الصائم محکم نھارانی شھر رمضان ص۳۳۰ نمبر ۲۳۶۷ متر مندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی کراھیة الحجامة للصائم ،ص۱۹۴، نمبر ۷۷۴ بخاری شریف ، باب الحجامة والقی للصائم ،نمبر (۱۹۳۸) یعنی روزہ ٹوٹنے کے قریب ہو گیا، اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔ لغت : الفصد : پچھلے زمانے میں رگ کاٹ کر مردہ خود نکالتے تھے اس کو فصد کہتے ہیں۔ الحجامہ : گردن کے اندرسوراخ کر کے منہ سے خون چوستے اور اس کو نکالتے تھے اس کو حجامت کہتے ہیں۔
Section on what is disliked for the fasting person. (1102) And everything that one thinks weakens him, like phlebotomy and cupping. Translation: (1102) [7] And every thing that one thinks will weaken him, like phlebotomy and cupping. Explanation: Doing something that causes weakness while fasting is disliked, for example getting cupped or phlebotomized causes weakness, and it is possible that it breaks the fast, therefore this action is disliked. Proof: (1) A hadith has passed that cupping does not break the fast because blood comes out, not enters the body. The hadith is: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet said: Three things do not break the fast of the fasting person: cupping, vomiting, and nocturnal emission. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Bukhari) This hadith shows that cupping does not break the fast. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet got cupped while fasting. (Bukhari) This shows the fast is not broken. (3) But there is another hadith that cupping breaks the fast: From Thawban from the Prophet: The cupper and the cupped have broken their fast. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Bukhari) Meaning the fast nearly broke, therefore it is disliked. Language: al-fasd: in ancient times they cut a vein to extract stagnant blood; al-hijama: making an incision in the neck and sucking out blood with the mouth.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It addresses actions that are disliked (makruh) for the fasting person due to weakness, specifically cupping (hijama) and phlebotomy (fasd). The author first states the ruling: anything that one believes weakens him is disliked. Then he explains that cupping and phlebotomy cause weakness and may lead to breaking the fast, hence they are disliked. He then provides three hadith proofs: (1) The hadith that cupping, vomiting, and nocturnal emission do not break the fast, indicating that cupping itself does not invalidate the fast. (2) The Prophet himself got cupped while fasting, confirming permissibility. (3) Another hadith that the cupper and cupped break their fast. The author reconciles these by stating that the third hadith indicates the fast nearly breaks, so it is disliked (karahah tanzihiyyah). In the Hanafi school, cupping is not a nullifier but is makruh because it weakens the body and may lead to breaking the fast. The passage ends with linguistic definitions of fasd and hijama.

Key Terms
الفصد (al-fasd): Cutting a vein to extract stagnant blood, a medical practice.
الحجامة (al-hijama): Making an incision on the neck and sucking out blood with the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is cupping (hijama) considered makruh during fasting?
A) Because it always breaks the fast.
B) Because it weakens the fasting person and may lead to breaking the fast.
C) Because it is a form of medical treatment that is prohibited.
D) Because it involves letting blood, which is impure.

Key Takeaway
Cupping and phlebotomy do not invalidate the fast but are disliked because they weaken the fasting person, based on reconciling conflicting hadith.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner

Nine Acts Not Disliked for the Fasting Person
Enumeration of nine permissible acts with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine actions that are not disliked for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, nine common acts—kissing, oiling, kohl, cupping, miswak, etc.—are not disliked; miswak is sunnah even at day's end.

Many Muslims wonder if everyday actions like using miswak or applying kohl are allowed while fasting. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: these acts are permissible and even recommended in the case of miswak. This lesson enumerates the nine actions with their supporting proofs from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the Nine Actions
From the passage, list all nine items: kissing, embracing, oil on mustache, kohl, cupping, phlebotomy, miswak, mouth rinsing, and bathing/cooling with wet clothes.
2
Identify Conditions and Hukm
For each action, note any condition (e.g., security from arousal for kissing) and its ruling (mubah for most, sunnah for miswak).
The passage explicitly states 'mufta bih' at the end, indicating the relied-upon position.
3
Examine the Hadith Proofs
For each action, locate the hadith or athar cited. For example, miswak: hadith from Bukhari and others showing the Prophet used miswak while fasting.
The passage adduces multiple proofs for miswak to emphasize its sunnah status.
4
Understand the Cross-Madhhab Dispute on Miswak
Note that some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider miswak after noon as makruh, but the Hanafi position is that it remains sunnah. The passage confirms the mufta bih is the latter.
This difference stems from varying interpretations of hadith about the fasting person's breath.

And nine things are not disliked for the fasting person: (1103) Kissing and fondling with security. (1104) Oil on the mustache and kohl. And 9 things that are not disliked for the fasting person: at a glance... kissing, embracing the wife when there is security from arousal... oil on the mustache. (☆☆☆) Cupping, phlebotomy - and using miswak until evening, rather it is sunnah. Rinsing the mouth or putting water in the nose without wudu. Bathing for cooling or wrapping in wet clothes. Translation: (1103) [1] Kissing. [2] Embracing the wife when there is security from arousal. Section: What is not disliked for the fasting person. Explanation: If one has control such that kissing or embracing will not lead to ejaculation, then kissing or embracing the wife is not disliked. The hadith has passed. Translation: (1104) [3] Applying oil to the mustache. [4] Applying kohl is not disliked. Reasoning: (1) Applying kohl is permissible; there is this hadith: Anas ibn Malik reported: A man came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said: My eyes are sore; should I apply kohl while I am fasting? He said: Yes. (Tirmidhi, chapter on kohl for the fasting person, p.154 no.726). (2) This hadith shows that kohl does not break the fast: Aisha said: Perhaps the Prophet (ﷺ) applied kohl while fasting. (Bayhaqi, chapter on the fasting person applying kohl, vol.4 p.437 no.8259). (3) There is also this athar: Anas ibn Malik used to apply kohl while fasting. (Abu Dawud, chapter on kohl at bedtime, book of fasting p.330 no.2378). This hadith and athar show that kohl does not break the fast. (4) And applying oil is recommended; there is this athar: Qatada said: It is recommended for the fasting person to apply oil so that the dusty appearance of the fasting person goes away. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on oil for the fasting person, vol.4 p.243 no.7942). This athar indicates that the fasting person should apply oil to look good. Translation: (1105) [5] Cupping. [6] Phlebotomy. Explanation: If there is no fear of weakness, then undergoing cupping and phlebotomy is not disliked. Reasoning: (1) Undergoing cupping while fasting is not disliked; the evidence is this hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet (ﷺ) was cupped while he was fasting. (Bukhari, chapter on cupping and vomiting for the fasting person, no.1939). This hadith shows that the Prophet underwent cupping while fasting. Translation: (1106) [7] Using miswak until the end of the day, rather it is sunnah like at the beginning, even if the miswak is wet or soaked in water. Explanation: Using miswak while fasting is sunnah, whether it is wet or soaked in water, and it is permissible in the morning and also permissible in the evening. Reasoning: (1) This hadith proves it: Amir ibn Rabi'a said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) using a miswak while he was fasting. Musaddad added: I cannot count how many times. (Abu Dawud, chapter on miswak for the fasting person, p.1344 no.2364; Tirmidhi, chapter on miswak for the fasting person, p.184 no.725; Bukhari, chapter on wet and dry miswak for the fasting person, p.1310 no.1934). This hadith shows that the Prophet used miswak while fasting. (2) Aisha reported: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: Among the best qualities of the fasting person is miswak. (Ibn Majah, chapter on miswak and kohl for the fasting person, p.240 no.1977). This hadith states that the best trait of a fasting person is using miswak, and it does not specify whether it is morning or evening, so using it in the evening is also better. (3) I asked Asim al-Ahwal: Should the fasting person use miswak? He said: Yes. I said: With a wet or dry miswak? He said: Yes. I said: At the beginning of the day or the end? He said: Yes. I said: From whom? He said: From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (ﷺ). (Darqutni, chapter on miswak for the fasting person, vol.2 p.182 no.2341; Bayhaqi, chapter on miswak for the fasting person, vol.4 p.452 no.8327). This hadith indicates that miswak can be used at the beginning of the day and at the end of the day. (4) Ibn Umar said: He used miswak at the beginning of the day and the end, and he did not swallow his saliva. (Bukhari, chapter on rinsing for the fasting person, p.1310 no.1930). This saying of a Companion indicates using miswak at both ends of the day. Translation: (1107) [8] Rinsing the mouth or putting water in the nose without wudu. [9] Bathing for cooling or wrapping in wet clothes. The mufta bih (relied-upon ruling).
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of nine actions that are not disliked (makruh) for a person observing a voluntary or obligatory fast according to the Hanafi school. The author lists them with supporting hadith and athar (traditions of the Companions). The commentary explains the conditions and rationale.

1. Kissing and fondling one's wife are not disliked provided there is security from arousal (i.e., one has control and there is no fear of ejaculation or engaging in intercourse). This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
2. Applying oil to the mustache and applying kohl (surma) to the eyes are both permissible. Kohl does not break the fast, and it is recommended to apply oil to avoid a dusty appearance.
3. Cupping (hijama) and phlebotomy (fasd) are not disliked as long as there is no danger of weakness. The Prophet underwent cupping while fasting.
4. Using the miswak (toothstick) throughout the day, even at the end of the day, is sunnah (recommended), whether the miswak is wet or dry. This is proven by multiple hadith.
5. Rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose without wudu are allowed; they do not invalidate the fast unless water is swallowed.
6. Bathing for cooling or wrapping oneself in wet clothes to beat the heat is permissible.

The author provides detailed proofs from hadith sources such as Bukhari, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Bayhaqi, and others. The overall ruling is that these actions are mubah (permissible) or sunnah (in the case of miswak), and they do not detract from the fast.

Key Terms
مکروه (makruh): Acts that are disliked; avoiding them is rewarded but doing them is not sinful.
سنت (sunnah): Recommended act established by the Prophet's practice; reward for doing, no sin for leaving.
سواک (siwak / miswak): Toothstick used for cleaning teeth; sunnah for the fasting person at all times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, using miswak at the end of the day for a fasting person is:
A) Makruh
B) Haram
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits nine actions during fasting, including kissing, oiling, kohl, cupping, and miswak—with miswak being sunnah even at the end of the day.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Miswak for the Fasting Person: Sunnah at Any Time
Ruling that miswak is sunnah for the fasting person at any time, with multiple hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on miswak use during fasting and identify the key hadith proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Using miswak while fasting is sunnah muakkadah at any time, even with a wet stick, according to the Hanafi school.

Many fasting individuals wonder whether using a miswak—especially a wet one—is allowed. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: it is a highly recommended sunnah at all times of the day, including the evening. We will explore the solid hadith evidence that establishes this ruling and address common misconceptions about wetness and timing.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the act (using miswak while fasting) and its hukm level (sunnah muakkadah). Note that it is recommended, not obligatory.
The text explicitly says 'بل هو سنة' (rather it is sunnah).
2
Examine the conditions
Understand that the ruling applies regardless of whether the miswak is wet or dry, and at any time of day (morning or evening).
The author states 'اگر چہ مسواک گیلی ہو یا پانی میں بھیگی ہو' (even if the miswak is wet or soaked in water).
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
Look at each of the four narrations cited: the practice of the Prophet, his statement, the report from Anas, and the statement of Ibn Umar. Understand how each serves as evidence.
The hadiths are direct or indirect evidence for the recommendation.
4
Contrast with opposing views
Note that some schools (e.g., Maliki) consider miswak disliked after midday. Compare their evidence (avoiding possible nullification) with the Hanafi reliance on general sunnah.
The Hanafi position prevails in the school based on stronger textual evidence.

Translation (106) [7] And using miswak until the evening, rather it is sunnah like the beginning of the day, even if the miswak is wet or soaked in water.
Explanation: Using miswak during fasting is sunnah, whether it is wet or made wet by soaking, and it is permissible in the morning and evening.
Proof: (1) This hadith is evidence: From Amir ibn Rabi'ah, he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah using a miswak while he was fasting. Musaddad added: more than I can count. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Miswak for the Fasting Person, p. 1344, no. 2364; Tirmidhi, Chapter on Miswak for the Fasting Person, p. 184, no. 725; Bukhari, Chapter on Wet and Dry Miswak for the Fasting Person, p. 1310, no. 1934) In this hadith, the Prophet would use miswak while fasting. (2) From A'ishah, she said: The Messenger of Allah said: Among the best qualities of a fasting person is the miswak. (Ibn Majah, Chapter on Miswak and Kohl for the Fasting Person, p. 240, no. 1977) This hadith states that the best characteristic of a fasting person is to use miswak, and it does not specify morning or evening, so using it in the evening is also good. (3) I asked 'Asim al-Ahwal: Does the fasting person use miswak? He said: Yes. I said: With a wet or dry miswak? He said: Yes. I said: At the beginning of the day or the end? He said: Yes. I said: From whom? He said: From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet. (Darqutni, Chapter on Miswak for the Fasting Person, vol. 2, p. 182, no. 2341; Bayhaqi, Chapter on Miswak for the Fasting Person, vol. 4, p. 452, no. 8327) This hadith states that one may use miswak both at the beginning and end of the day. (4) Ibn 'Umar said: He uses miswak at the beginning and end of the day, and does not swallow his saliva. (Bukhari, Chapter on the Fasting Person Rinsing, p. 1310, no. 1930) This Companion saying indicates using miswak at both times.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses the ruling on using a miswak (tooth-stick) while fasting. The Hanafi position, as presented here, is that using a miswak is sunnah (recommended) for the fasting person at any time of day, including the evening. This applies whether the miswak is wet or dry. The proof includes multiple hadiths: the Prophet himself used miswak while fasting, and he stated that using miswak is among the best qualities of a fasting person. The text also records a companion saying that Ibn 'Umar used miswak at both ends of the day. The author emphasizes that there is no distinction between morning and evening, so using it in the evening is also commendable. This counters the misconception that miswak is disliked later in the day due to the possibility of swallowing moisture. The Hanafi school considers it permissible and recommended.

Key Terms
سواك (siwak): A twig used for cleaning teeth, also called miswak. In fasting, it is sunnah to use it at any time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only if the miswak is dry.

D) Only when not fasting.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that using a miswak is a sunnah act at any time during the fast, regardless of wetness or time of day, provided one does not swallow anything.

Rinsing, Bathing, and Wet Cloths Not Disliked for Fasting Person
Ruling that rinsing, sniffing water, bathing, and using wet cloths for cooling are permissible for fasting person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rinsing the mouth, sniffing water, bathing, and using wet cloths during fasting, and cite the supporting proofs.

Core Idea
External water use during fasting does not break the fast; only swallowing does.

Many assume that any water contact during fasting invalidates it, but the Hanafi school specifies that external actions like rinsing, bathing, or using a wet cloth are permissible as long as water is not swallowed. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions discussed
List the actions: rinsing mouth (madmadah), sniffing water (istinshaq) without wudu, bathing (ghusl), and wrapping in a wet cloth (talaffuf) for cooling.
All involve external water contact, not swallowing.
2
Ascertain the ruling per Hanafi school
The mufta bihi (relied-upon fatwa) is that these actions are permissible and not disliked (makruh). The hukm level is mubah.
No difference within the school; it's permissible.
3
Examine the proofs (dalil)
For each action, find the proof: (a) Statement of al-Hasan al-Basri for rinsing; (b) Hadith: 'Sniff water deeply unless you are fasting' for istinshaq; (c) Aishah's hadith about the Prophet bathing while fasting; (d) Hadith of pouring water on head for cooling.
The proofs are from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
4
Understand the critical condition
The key limitation: water must not be swallowed intentionally. If swallowed, the fast breaks. The external use is safe.
This aligns with the general principle that water entering the body through the throat invalidates fast.

...wet with water (117) And rinsing the mouth and sniffing water without wudu, and bathing, and wrapping oneself in a wet cloth for cooling, according to the fatwa. (1108) And three things are recommended for him: suhur, delaying it, and hastening the breaking of the fast on a day without clouds.
Explanation: If he is not performing wudu and only puts water in his nose or rinses his mouth, it is also permissible; sometimes this is necessary to moisten the mouth. Bathing or soaking a cloth and placing it on the body is permissible to cool down.
Proof: (1) Al-Hasan said: There is no harm in rinsing the mouth and cooling down for the fasting person. (Bukhari, Chapter on the Fasting Person Rinsing, p. 310, no. 1930) This statement of a Successor indicates that rinsing for cooling is permissible. (2) From his father Laqit ibn Sabirah, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: Sniff water deeply unless you are fasting. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Fasting Person Pouring Water on Himself and Sniffing Deeply, p. 1344, no. 2366) This hadith states that a fasting person may put water in his nose but should not sniff deeply. (3) Bathing is permissible; for this there is this hadith: A'ishah said: The Prophet would reach dawn in Ramadan in a state of janabah without a wet dream, then he would bathe and fast. (Bukhari, Chapter on the Fasting Person Rinsing, p. 1310, no. 1930) (4) Pouring water over the head to cool down is permissible; for this there is this hadith: From Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Rahman from some companions of the Prophet, he said: I saw the Prophet ordering the people in his journey during the year of the conquest to break the fast, saying 'Be strong for your enemy,' and the Messenger of Allah fasted. Abu Bakr said: The one who narrated to me said: I saw the Messenger of Allah at al-Arj pouring water over his head while fasting due to thirst or heat. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Fasting Person Pouring Water on Himself and Sniffing Deeply, p. 1344, no. 2365) This hadith states that a fasting person can pour water over his head.
Vocabulary: Talfuf: derived from laff, to wrap. Muttabil: derived from ball, to be wet.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings related to water use during fasting. The Hanafi position, as given, is that rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water (istinshaq) without wudu is permissible for the fasting person, as is bathing (ghusl) and wrapping oneself in a wet cloth to cool down. These actions do not break the fast. The proofs include a statement from al-Hasan al-Basri, a hadith allowing water for cooling, the practice of the Prophet bathing while fasting after janabah, and a specific hadith about pouring water on the head. The author notes the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) is that these are not disliked. The commentary also provides vocabulary explanations. This reinforces that using water externally for cooling or cleanliness is allowed, whereas swallowing water would break the fast.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth without swallowing; permissible for the fasting person.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose; permissible but without exaggeration during fasting.
تلفّف (talaffuf): Wrapping oneself in a wet cloth for cooling; permissible for the fasting person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
External water use (rinsing, sniffing, bathing, wet cloths) is permissible during fasting; only intentional swallowing breaks the fast.

Recommended Acts for the Fasting Person: Suhur, Delaying Suhur, and Hastening Iftar
Listing three recommended acts with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended acts for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Suhur brings blessing; delaying it strengthens the fast; hastening iftar follows the Prophet's practice.

The fasting person is encouraged to follow the Prophetic guidance regarding the pre-dawn meal and the breaking of the fast. This lesson identifies three mustahabb acts—eating suhur, delaying it near dawn, and hastening iftar on clear days—and the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the three acts mentioned and their legal classification.
All three are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited in the passage.
The hadith from Bukhari: 'Eat suhur, for in suhur there is blessing.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith indicates recommendation.
The imperative 'tashahharu' signals a non-obligatory command, and the mention of blessing shows virtue.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check for any disagreement among madhahib.
Generally agreed upon; delaying suhur is specific to Hanafi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Confirm the mufta bihi position.
The relied-upon position is that all three are mustahabb.

(۱۱۰۸) ويستحب له ثلاثة اشياء السحور وتاخيره وتعجيل الفطر في غير يوم قول۔
ترجمه : (۱۱۰۸) روزه دار کے لئے تین چیزیں مستحب ہیں:
سحری۔
..... اور اس کو مؤخر کرنا ۔
اور افطار میں جلدی کرنا جس دن بادل نہ ہو۔
تشریح : سحری کرنا اور اس کو صبح صادق کے قریب کھانا ، یہ مستحب ہے تا کہ روزے پر قوت حاصل کر سکے۔ اور جس دن بادل نہ ہوتو افطار میں جلدی کرنا مستحب ہے، اور بادل ہو تو تو دیر کرے تاکہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ سورج ڈوبنے سے پہلے ہی افطار کر لیا۔
وجه : (۱) - سمعت انس بن مالك قال قال النبي لالالالالاله تسحروا فان في السحور بركة . (بخارى شريف،
(1108) And three things are recommended for him: suhur, delaying it, and hastening the breaking of the fast on a day without clouds?
Translation: (1108) Three things are recommended for the fasting person: Suhur, and delaying it, and hastening the breaking of the fast on a day without clouds.
Explanation: Eating suhur and eating it close to dawn is recommended so that he gains strength for the fast. On a day without clouds, hastening the breaking of the fast is recommended, and if there are clouds, he should delay so that he does not break his fast before sunset.
Proof: (1) I heard Anas ibn Malik say: The Prophet said: Eat suhur, for in suhur there is blessing. (Bukhari, ...)
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage presents the recommended (mustahabb) acts for the fasting person according to the Hanafi school. Three key actions are highlighted: (1) Having suhur (the pre-dawn meal), (2) Delaying suhur until close to dawn (fajr sadiq), and (3) Hastening to break the fast (iftar) when the sky is clear. The reasoning for delaying suhur is to gain strength for the day's fast. For iftar, hastening is recommended on clear days to ensure the sun has actually set; on cloudy days, one should delay slightly to avoid breaking the fast prematurely. The evidence provided is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik (though cut off in the OCR) emphasizing the blessing in suhur. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on following the prophetic practice and taking precautions in ibadah.

Key Terms
سحور (suhur): The pre-dawn meal before starting the fast; recommended (mustahabb) in Hanafi fiqh.
افطار (iftar): Breaking the fast at sunset; hastening it is recommended on clear days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Hastening iftar on a clear day.

Key Takeaway
The three recommended acts (suhur, delaying suhur, hastening iftar) follow the Prophetic guidance and bring blessing and ease to the fast.

Permissible Acts During Fasting: Cooling and Hygiene
Ruling with evidence on permissible acts during fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four acts that are permissible (not disliked) for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school, and cite the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Rinsing, sniffing, bathing, and wet cloth are permissible — only swallowing water matters.

In this lesson, we examine four actions that many assume break the fast but are in fact completely permissible: rinsing the mouth, sniffing water up the nose without exaggeration, taking a bath, and cooling oneself with a wet cloth. These rulings are based on clear hadith evidence and are the relied-upon position (mufta bih) in the Hanafi school. Understanding this helps avoid unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions
List the four acts mentioned in the passage that are ruled as 'not disliked' (ma la yukrah): madmadah (mouth rinsing), istinshaq (sniffing water) without wudu, ghusl (bathing), and talfuf bi thawb mubtall (wrapping in wet cloth).
The qualifier 'li ghayr wudu' indicates these are done independently, not as part of ablution.
2
Locate the proof for each act
For each act, find the corresponding hadith or athar cited: (1) Hasan al-Basri's statement for rinsing/cooling, (2) hadith of Laqit for sniffing, (3) hadith of Aisha for bathing, (4) hadith of companions for pouring water on head.
The proofs are a mix of prophetic hadith and companion/taabi'ee statements.
3
Understand the Hanafi principle
The underlying principle is that only intentional swallowing of water (or other substances) invalidates the fast. External contact with water does not break the fast.
This explains why these acts are permissible: they do not involve swallowing.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab context
Note that some other schools consider these acts makruh. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit wording of the proofs (e.g., 'la ba's' and 'the Prophet poured water') to permit them.
The passage marks the position as 'ala al-mufta bih' (the relied-upon fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما لا تكره للصائم
المضمضة والاستنشاق لغير وضوء والاغتسال والتلفّف بثوب مبتل للتبرد على المفتى به.
تشريح : وضو نہیں کر رہا ہے اور صرف ناک میں پانی ڈالتا ہے، یا کل کرتا ہے تب بھی جائز ہے، بعض مرتبہ منہ تر کرنے کے لئے ایسا کرنا پڑتا ہے۔ ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے لئے غسل کرنا، یا کپڑا بھگا کر جسم پر رکھنا جائز ہے۔
وجه : (ا) قال الحسن لا بأس بالمضمضة و التبرد للصائم ۔ (بخاری شریف، باب التسال الصائم ، ص۳۱۰ ، نمبر ۱۹۳۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے لئے کلی کرنا جائز ہے۔ (۲) عن ابیه لقيط بن صبرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالغ فى الاستنشاق الا ان يكون صائما - ابوداود شریف، باب الصائم يصب عليه الماء من العطش و يبالغ في الاستنشاق، ص ۱۳۴۴، نمبر ۲۳۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روزہ دار ناک میں پانی ڈال سکتا ہے ، لیکن مبالغہ نہ کرے (۳) غسل کرنا جائز ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ قالت عائشة كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يدركه الفجر جنبا في رمضان من غير حلم فيغتسل و يصوم . (بخاری شریف ، باب انتسال الصائم ، ص ۱۳۱۰، نمبر ۱۹۳۰) (۴) ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے . لئے سر پر پانی ڈالنا جائز ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی بکر بن عبد الرحمن عن بعض اصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال رأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم امر الناس في سفره عام الفتح بالفطر و قال تقووا لعدوكم ، و صام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ابوبكر قال الذى حدثني لقد رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالعرج يصب على رأسه الماء و هو صائم من العطش او من الحر ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الصائم يصب عليه الماء من العطش ويبالغ في الاستنشاق ،ص ۱۳۴۴، نمبر ۲۳۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روزہ دار سر پر پانی ڈال سکتا ہے۔
لغت: تللف : لف سے مشتق ہے، لیٹنا ۔ متل : بل سے مشتق ہے، تر ہونا۔
What is not disliked for the fasting person: rinsing the mouth and sniffing water without wudu, washing, and wrapping oneself in a wet cloth for cooling - according to the relied-upon position. Commentary: He is not performing wudu and simply puts water in his nose, or rinses his mouth - that too is permissible. Sometimes one needs to do this to moisten the mouth. To cool down, washing or soaking a cloth and placing it on the body is permissible. Evidence: (1) Al-Hasan said: There is no harm in rinsing the mouth and cooling down for the fasting person. (Bukhari, chapter on the fasting person's rubbing, no. 1930) This statement of a Tabi'i is that rinsing the mouth to cool down is permissible. (2) From his father Laqit ibn Sabirah said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Exaggerate in sniffing water unless you are fasting. (Abu Dawud, chapter on the fasting person pouring water due to thirst and exaggerating in sniffing, no. 2366) This hadith states that a fasting person can put water in his nose, but should not exaggerate. (3) Washing is permissible; for it there is this hadith: Aisha said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) would wake up for Fajr in Ramadan in a state of janabah without a wet dream, then wash and fast. (Bukhari, chapter on the fasting person's washing, no. 1930) (4) Pouring water on the head to cool down is permissible; for it there is this hadith: From Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Rahman from some companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) order the people during his journey in the year of the conquest to break the fast and said: Be strong for your enemy. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) fasted. Abu Bakr said: The one who told me said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at al-Arj pouring water over his head while he was fasting due to thirst or heat. (Abu Dawud, chapter on the fasting person pouring water due to thirst and exaggerating in sniffing, no. 2365) This hadith states that a fasting person can pour water over his head. Vocabulary: Talfuf: derived from laffa, to lie down. Mubtall: derived from balla, to be wet.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs. The author begins by listing four actions that are not disliked (makruh) for a fasting person: rinsing the mouth, sniffing water up the nose without performing wudu, taking a full bath (ghusl), and wrapping oneself in a wet cloth for cooling. The phrase 'ala al-mufta bih indicates that this is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies that these actions are permissible even if one is not doing wudu—for example, simply wetting the mouth or nose. The author then provides four evidences: (1) a statement of Hasan al-Basri (a Tabi'i) that there is no harm in rinsing the mouth and cooling down for the fasting person; (2) a hadith from Laqit ibn Sabirah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed to exaggerate in sniffing water except when fasting, proving that sniffing without exaggeration is allowed; (3) a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet would sometimes be in a state of janabah at Fajr and would take a bath and fast, proving that washing does not break the fast; (4) a hadith from some companions that the Prophet poured water on his head while fasting due to thirst or heat, proving that cooling the body with water is permissible. The vocabulary section explains two words: talfuf (wrapping) and mubtall (wet).

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water without swallowing.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose.
التلفّف بثوب مبتل (al-talfuf bi thawb mubtall): Wrapping oneself in a wet cloth to cool down.
تلّف (talfuf): Wrapping or enfolding.
مبتل (mubtall): Wet, moistened.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Using a miswak without moisture
B) Taking a bath (ghusl) due to janabah
C) Rinsing the mouth without swallowing water
D) Sniffing water without exaggerating

Key Takeaway
Rinsing, sniffing (without exaggeration), bathing, and cooling with wet cloth are all permissible for the fasting person, based on direct prophetic practice and statements.

Three Recommended Acts for the Fasting Person
Ruling with evidence on three mustahabb acts during fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three mustahabb acts for a fasting person according to the Hanafi school and explain the exception for a cloudy day, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Suhur, delaying it, and hastening iftar are recommended — but delay iftar on a cloudy day to avoid error.

This lesson covers three recommended practices for the fasting person: eating suhur (pre-dawn meal), delaying suhur to just before dawn, and hastening iftar (breaking the fast) immediately after sunset, except when clouds obscure the sunset. The Hanafi school relies on several hadith and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to establish these as sunnah muakkadah. Understanding these recommendations helps avoid common mistakes such as thinking suhur is obligatory or breaking the fast too early on a cloudy day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
From the opening sentence, list exactly what actions are recommended (mustahabb) for the fasting person according to the Hanafi tradition.
The three are: having suhur, delaying suhur (i.e., eating close to dawn), and hastening iftar (breaking fast immediately after sunset).
2
Locate the exception
Read the condition 'fi ghayr yawm ghaym' (except on a cloudy day). Understand why the ruling for hastening iftar is modified on a cloudy day.
The purpose is to ensure the sun has actually set, avoiding accidental eating before Maghrib.
3
Examine the first proof
Analyze the hadith 'Tasahharu fa inna fi al-sahuri barakah'. Observe how the imperative is used and how the Hanafi school understands it as recommendation, not obligation (min ghayr ijab).
This hadith from Bukhari and Muslim establishes suhur as a blessed sunnah.
4
Examine the second and third proofs
Study the hadith from Aisha showing the Prophet's practice of hastening iftar and delaying suhur, and the hadith about Bilal and Ibn Umm Maktum indicating the time limit for suhur.
These emphasize the prophetic model (kadhalika kana yaf'alu) and clarify the window for suhur.
5
Examine the fourth proof
Review the athar from Abu Darda linking these actions to the character of the prophets (akhlaq al-nabiyyin). Consider its role as supplementary evidence.
This reinforces the ethical and spiritual dimension of these practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب له ثلاثة اشياء السحور وتاخيره وتعجيل الفطر في غير يوم غيم.
تشريح : سحری کرنا اور اس کو صبح صادق کے قریب کھانا ، یہ مستحب ہے تا کہ روزے پر قوت حاصل کر سکے۔ اور جس دن بادل نہ ہوتو افطار میں جلدی کرنا مستحب ہے، اور بادل ہو تو تو دیر کرے تاکہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ سورج ڈوبنے سے پہلے ہی افطار کر لیا۔
وجه : (۱) - سمعت انس بن مالك قال قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تسحروا فان في السحور بركة . (بخارى شريف، باب برکت السحور من غیر ایجاب ،ص ۳۰۹ نمبر ۱۹۲۳ر مسلم شریف، باب فضل السحور رو تا کید استقبا به ص ۴۴۷، نمبر ۲۵۴۹/۱۰۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سحری کرو اس میں برکت ہے ۔ (۲) تاخیر سے سحری کرے اور جلدی افطار کرے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے
صلى الله
قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى عائشة فقلنا يا أم المؤمنين ان فينا رجلين من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أما أحدهما فيعجل الافطار و يؤخر السحور و أما الآخر فيؤخر الافطار و يعجل السحور فقالت من هذا الذي يعجل الافطار و
يؤخر السحور قلنا ابن مسعود قالت كذالك كان يفعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( سنن بیہقی ، باب ما يستحب من تجميل الفطر وتأخير السحور، ج رابع ، ص ۴۴۰، نمبر ۸۱۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سحری کو تاخیر سے کرنا بہتر ہے، لیکن اتنی تاخیر نہ کرے کہ صبح صادق ہو جائے ۔ (۳) عن عائشة أن بلالا كان يؤذن بليل فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم له : كلوا و اشربوا حتى يؤذن ابن ام مـكـتـوم فانه لا يؤذن حتى يطلع الفجر قال القاسم و لم يكن بين اذانهما الا أن يرقى اذا و ينزل ذا ( بخاری شریف ، باب قول النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يمنعنكم من سحور كم اذان بلال ، ص ۳۰۸، نمبر ۱۹۱۸ر مسلم شریف ، باب بیان ان الدخول فی الصوم تحصل بطلوع الفجر، الخ، ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۲۵۳۸/۱۰۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر طلوع ہونے تک سحری کر سکتا ہے۔ (۴) عن ابي درداء قال : من أخلاق النبيين : التبكير في الافطار و الابلاغ في السحور و وضع اليمين على
الشمال في الصلوة . (مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب فی تعبیل الافطار و ماذکر فیہ، ج ثانی ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۸۹۵۷/مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب تأخیر السحور ، ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۷۶۴۵ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ افطار جلدی کرنا اور سحری میں تاخیر کرنا نبیوں کے اخلاق میں سے ہے۔
And three things are recommended for him: suhur (pre-dawn meal), delaying it, and hastening iftar (breaking the fast) except on a cloudy day. Commentary: To eat suhur and to eat it close to dawn (subh sadiq) is recommended, so that one gains strength for the fast. And on a day without clouds, it is recommended to hasten iftar, but if there are clouds then delay so that one does not break the fast before sunset. Evidence: (1) I heard Anas ibn Malik say: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Eat suhur, for indeed in suhur there is blessing. (Bukhari, chapter on the blessing of suhur without obligation, p. 309 no. 1923; Muslim, chapter on the virtue of suhur and the emphasis on it, p. 447 no. 2549/1095) This hadith shows that one should eat suhur; there is blessing in it. (2) That one should delay suhur and hasten iftar; its evidence is this hadith: We entered upon Aisha and said: O Mother of the Believers, there are two men among the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him). One hastens iftar and delays suhur, and the other delays iftar and hastens suhur. She asked: Who is this who hastens iftar and delays suhur? We said: Ibn Mas'ud. She said: That is what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to do. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is recommended of hastening iftar and delaying suhur, vol. 4 p. 440 no. 8122) This hadith shows that delaying suhur is better, but not to such an extent that dawn comes. (3) From Aisha: That Bilal used to give the adhan at night, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives the adhan, for he does not give the adhan until dawn breaks. Al-Qasim said: There was no interval between their adhans except that one would ascend and the other descend. (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's saying: Do not let Bilal's adhan prevent you from your suhur, p. 308 no. 1918; Muslim, vol. 1 p. 445 no. 2538/1092) This hadith shows that one can eat suhur until dawn. (4) From Abu Darda: He said: Among the characteristics of the prophets are: hastening iftar, prolonging suhur, and placing the right hand on the left in prayer. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on hastening iftar and what is mentioned therein, vol. 2 p. 279 no. 8957; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on delaying suhur, p. 178 no. 7645) This effect shows that hastening iftar and delaying suhur are from the character of the prophets.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on three mustahabb (recommended) actions for a fasting person: taking suhur, delaying suhur (i.e., eating it just before dawn), and hastening iftar (breaking the fast immediately after sunset), except on a cloudy day. The commentary (tashrih) explains the wisdom: suhur provides strength for the fast; delaying it makes it closer to dawn; hastening iftar is recommended unless the sky is cloudy, because one needs to be certain that the sun has set. The author then provides four proofs: (1) The well-known hadith 'Eat suhur, for in suhur there is blessing' from Bukhari and Muslim, indicating it is a sunnah without obligation. (2) A hadith from Aisha showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to hasten iftar and delay suhur, as reported by Bayhaqi. (3) A hadith about Bilal and Ibn Umm Maktum's adhans, indicating that suhur can be taken until Fajr time. (4) An athar from Abu Darda that these practices are from the character of the prophets. The passage emphasizes that these actions are recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
سحور (suhur): The pre-dawn meal eaten before the Fajr adhan during Ramadan.
إفطار (iftar): Breaking the fast at sunset.
غيم (ghaym): Cloudy sky, which may cause uncertainty about sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Suhur, delaying it, and hastening iftar are strongly recommended sunnah acts for the fasting person, with the exception that on a cloudy day one should delay iftar to be certain of sunset.
