ترجمه (۱۱۷) اور شیخ فانی اور فاضیہ بڑھیا کے لئے افطار جائز ہے، اور ان دونوں پر فدیہ دینا لازم ہے ہر دن ( کے روزے کے بدلے میں ) آدھا صاع گیہوں۔ تشریح : ایسا بوڑھایا بوڑھی جو روزہ نہیں رکھ سکتا ہو اور آئندہ بھی رکھنے کی امید نہ ہو تو اس پر روزہ واجب ہے لیکن نہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے اس پر فدیہ لازم کیا گیا ہے کہ ہر دن کے بدلے ایک مسکین کو کھانا کھلائے ۔ کیونکہ اب رکھنے کی امید ہی نہیں ہے۔۔ اسی کو فانی بوڑھا، اور فانیہ بوڑھی، کہتے ہیں۔ وجه (1) آیت میں ہے۔ وعلى الذين يطيقونه فدية طعام مسكين فمن تطوع خيرا فهو خير له و ان تصوموا خير لكم ان كنتم تعلمون ( آیت ۱۸۴، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲)، اور اس کا معنی یہ فرمایا کہ روزے کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو۔(۲) قول صحابی میں ہے . سمع ابن عباس يقول وعلى الذين يطيقونه فدية طعام مسكين قال ابن عباس لیست بمنسوخة ، هو الشيخ الكبير و المرأة الكبيرة لا يستطيعان أن يصوما ، فليطعمان مكان كل يوم مسكينا .( بخاری شریف ، باب قوله تعالی ایاما معدودات فمن کان منکم مریضا الخ ص ۵۶۶ نمبر ۴۵۰۵ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من قال هی مثبت للشیخ والحبلی ص ۱۳۳۸ نمبر ۲۳۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شیخ فانی قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ اور ہر دن کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں مسکین کو فدیہ دے گا۔(۳) عن ابن عباس انه كان يقرأها وعلى الذين يطيقونه ويقول هو الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يستطيع الصيام فيفطر ويطعم عن كل يوم مسكينا نصف صاع من حنطة (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الشيخ الكبير، ج رابع ، ص ۱۷۰ نمبر ۷۶۰۴ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شیخ فانی قضا نہیں کرے گا ۔ اور ہر دن کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں مسکین کو فدیہ دے گا۔ آدھا صاع گیہوں 1.769 کیلو ہوتا ہے، اس لئے 30 دن روزے کا فدیہ 53.07 کیلو ہوگا ۔ یعنی تیر پن کیلو اور سات گرام
Translation (117): And it is permissible for a very old man and an old woman to break their fast, and both are obligated to give fidya for each day: half a sa' of wheat. Explanation: An old man or woman who cannot fast and has no hope of being able to fast in the future: fasting is obligatory on them, but because they cannot, fidya is made obligatory for them: to feed a poor person for each day. Because there is no hope of being able to fast. They are called an old man (fani) and an old woman (fania). Evidence (1): The verse: 'And upon those who can bear it, a fidya: feeding a poor person.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:184), and its meaning has been explained as those who do not have the strength to fast. (2) A Companion's saying: Ibn Abbas heard and said: 'On those who can bear it: fidya of feeding a poor person.' Ibn Abbas said: 'It is not abrogated. It refers to the very old man and old woman who cannot fast. So let them feed a poor person for each day.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This athar shows that the very old person does not make up (qada), but gives half a sa' of wheat to a poor person for each day. (3) From Ibn Abbas: He used to recite it as 'those who can bear it' and said: 'It is the very old man who cannot fast, so he breaks his fast and feeds a poor person for each day half a sa' of wheat.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) This athar also shows that the very old person does not make up qada, but gives half a sa' of wheat to a poor person as fidya. Half a sa' of wheat is 1.769 kg, so for 30 days the fidya is 53.07 kg (i.e., 53 kg and 7 grams).
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the exemption of a very elderly person (sheikh fani or ajuz fania) who is permanently unable to fast due to old age and has no hope of recovery. The author states that such a person may break the fast (i.e., is not required to fast) but must pay fidya: half a sa' of wheat per missed day. The explanation clarifies that even though fasting is originally obligatory, the inability makes the obligation convert to fidya. Three proofs are provided: first, the Quranic verse 2:184, which is interpreted by Ibn Abbas as referring to the elderly; second, the explicit statement of Ibn Abbas that the verse is not abrogated and applies to the very old; third, another narration specifying the amount (half a sa' of wheat). The author then gives the modern weight equivalence (1.769 kg per half sa') and calculates the total fidya for a full month. The Hanafi ruling is that qada is not required for such a person; fidya suffices and must be given before death if possible.

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): A very old man who has reached an age of extreme weakness and cannot fast, with no hope of improvement.
فدية (fidya): A compensatory meal given to a poor person for each missed obligatory fast due to permanent inability.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; half a sa' is approximately 1.769 kg of wheat in modern terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An 80-year-old man is unable to fast due to severe weakness and is not expected to recover. What does the Hanafi school require him to do?
A) He must fast as much as he can and make up the rest later.
B) He is excused entirely, no action needed.
C) He must pay fidya (half a sa' of wheat per day) for each missed day.
D) He must fast if possible, otherwise give fidya only if he was rich.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates fidya (half a sa' of wheat per day) for the elderly who permanently cannot fast, based on the Quran and Ibn Abbas's interpretation, with no qada required.

Ruling on Elderly Unable to Fast: Fidyah
Explains ruling for elderly who cannot fast, with Quran and Hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for an elderly person who cannot fast and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence that establishes it.

Core Idea
For the elderly who cannot fast permanently, fidyah replaces qada — half a sa' of wheat per missed day.

This lesson addresses a common situation: an elderly Muslim whose health prevents fasting, with no hope of recovery. The Hanafi school, based on Quran 2:184 and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas, provides a clear ruling: the fast is waived but a compensatory fidyah is wajib. We will examine the evidence and the precise amount required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on an elderly man (shaykh fani) and woman (ajuz faniya) who cannot fast. Fasting is originally wajib, but it is permissible to break the fast, and fidyah becomes wajib instead of qada.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The verse 'And upon those who are able to fast, a fidyah of feeding a miskeen' (Quran 2:184) is cited. The interpretation of Ibn Abbas applies this to the elderly who cannot fast.
The phrase 'yutiquunahu' is understood as 'cannot bear it' in this context.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two narrations from Ibn Abbas confirm that the verse is not abrogated and applies specifically to the elderly who cannot fast. They must feed a miskeen for each day.
The hadiths are from Bukhari and Abu Dawud, and also from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Determine the fidyah amount
The text specifies half a sa' of wheat per day. In modern terms, that is approximately 1.769 kg, so for 30 days it is about 53.07 kg.
A full sa' is 3.538 kg in this text.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools interpret 'yutiquunahu' as 'able to fast' and consider the fidyah ruling abrogated. The Hanafi school, following Ibn Abbas, maintains it as operative for the elderly.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

And it is permissible to break the fast for an elderly man and an elderly woman, and fidyah is obligatory upon them for every day, half a sa' of wheat. Translation (117): For the elderly man and the elderly woman, it is permissible to break the fast, and upon both of them, giving fidyah is obligatory for each day (in place of the fast) half a sa' of wheat. Explanation: An old man or woman who cannot fast and has no hope of being able to in the future—fasting is wajib upon them, but due to inability, fidyah is made obligatory: for each day, feed one miskeen. Because there is no hope of fasting. This is what is meant by fani old man and faniya old woman. Evidence (1) The verse: 'And upon those who are able to fast, a fidyah of feeding a miskeen...' (2) Saying of a Companion: Ibn Abbas said it is not abrogated; it is for the old man and old woman who cannot fast, so they feed a miskeen for each day. (3) From Ibn Abbas that he recited it and said it is for the old man who cannot fast, so he breaks the fast and feeds a miskeen half a sa' of wheat for each day. Half a sa' of wheat is 1.769 kg, so fidyah for 30 days is 53.07 kg, i.e., fifty-three kilos and seven grams of wheat.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with supporting evidence. The matn states that it is permissible for an elderly person (shaykh fani or ajuz faniya) to break the fast, and fidyah is obligatory: half a sa' of wheat per day. The sharh explains that this applies to those who cannot fast now and have no hope of recovery. Fasting is originally wajib, but due to permanent inability, fidyah substitutes. The proofs: Quran 2:184 interpreted as referring to those who cannot fast, and two athar from Ibn Abbas confirming the ruling and specifying half a sa' of wheat. The weight note provides modern equivalents: half sa' = 1.769 kg, thus 30 days fidyah = 53.07 kg wheat.

Key Terms
شیخ فانی (shaykh fani): An old man whose strength has declined to the point he cannot fast and has no hope of recovery.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation for missed fast by feeding a miskeen half a sa' of wheat per day.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, here equated to 3.538 kg of wheat.

Ruling on Vow of Perpetual Fasting When Unable
Ruling on inability in perpetual fasting vow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a valid vow of perpetual fasting when the vowholder becomes unable to fast due to livelihood, and explain the hierarchy of compensation (fidyah then istighfar).

Core Idea
A vow of perpetual fasting is binding but compensable: fidyah for each missed fast; if unable, seeking forgiveness suffices.

Vows (nathr) are generally binding in the Hanafi school, but the law accommodates genuine inability. This passage addresses the specific case of someone who vowed to fast every day (nadhral-ibad) but later finds it impossible due to the demands of earning a livelihood. It lays out a clear hierarchy: first break the fast and pay fidyah; if even fidyah is unaffordable, then seek Allah’s forgiveness. This ruling balances the obligation of the vow with the reality of human limitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is a vow of perpetual fasting (nadhral-ibad). The ruling: if unable due to livelihood, the vowholder may break the fast and must pay fidyah.
The fidyah is half a sa' of wheat per missed day.
2
Understand the Condition of Inability
The inability must be due to a valid excuse, here exemplified by 'preoccupation with livelihood' (al-ishtighal bil-ma'ishah). This is a legitimate reason that lifts the obligation to fast.
Other valid excuses may apply by analogy.
3
Apply the Compensation Hierarchy
First, pay fidyah for each missed day. If unable to pay due to poverty, the obligation shifts to seeking forgiveness (istighfar) and asking for absolution (istiqalah).
Fidyah is wajib; istighfar is the final resort.
4
Recognize the Legal Basis
The ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that vows are binding but subject to necessity. There is no explicit Quranic or hadith text for this specific case; it is derived from general maxims of ease and removal of hardship.
This ruling belongs to the later fatwa tradition (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
5
Note the Practical Distinction
Unlike obligatory (fard) fasts, a vow fast can be broken with compensation. This is because the vow is a voluntary act that becomes binding, but its obligation is less stringent than a divinely mandated fast.
The fidyah amount is the same as for the elderly who cannot fast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۱۸) کمن نذر صوم الابد فضعُف عنه لاشتغاله بالمعيشة يُفطر ويفدى فان لم يقدر على الفدية لعُسرته يستغفر الله تعالى ويستقيله .
ترجمه : (۱۱۸) اس طرح کہ جس شخص نے ہمیشہ روزہ رکھنے کی منت مان لی تھی پھر رزق کی مشغولی کی وجہ سے عاجز ہو گیا تو وہ افطار کرے اور فدیہ دیتا رہے،اگر افلاس کی وجہ سے فدیہ سے بھی عاجز ہو گیا تو استغفار کرتا رہے اور معافی مانگتا رہے۔ تشریح : یہ ایک مثال ہے۔ کسی نے ہمیشہ روزہ رکھنے کی منت مان لی لیکن روزی وغیرہ کی تلاش کی وجہ سے منت پوری نہ کر سکا، اور روزہ نہ رکھ سکا تو یہ روزہ نہ رکھے اور ہر دن کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں دیتا رہے، اور گیہوں بھی نہیں دے سکتا ہو تو اب استغفار کرے اور معافی مانگتا رہے۔
لغت : يستقيل : اقالہ سے مشتق ہے، اقالہ کرے، یعنی معافی مانگے ۔
(1118) Like one who vowed perpetual fasting then became weak for it due to preoccupation with livelihood, he breaks the fast and pays fidyah. If he cannot afford fidyah due to his poverty, he seeks forgiveness from Allah and asks for absolution. Translation: (118) For example, a person who vowed to fast forever then became unable due to seeking livelihood, so he breaks the fast and pays fidyah. If he is also unable to pay fidyah due to poverty, he keeps seeking forgiveness and asks for pardon. Explanation: This is an example. Someone vowed to fast forever but could not fulfill the vow due to earning a living, and could not fast. So he does not fast and instead gives half a sa' of wheat for each day. If he cannot even give wheat, then he seeks forgiveness and asks for pardon. Lexicon: yastaqil: derived from iqalah, meaning to seek pardon.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding a specific type of vow (nadhral-ibad). The matn states that if one vowed to fast perpetually (every day) but later becomes unable due to work, he may break the fast and pay fidyah (half sa' per day). If even fidyah is not possible due to poverty, he should seek Allah's forgiveness. The commentary explains that this is an example of a valid excuse. The fidyah amount is the same as for the elderly. The key point: the vow becomes non-binding to the extent of hardship, but compensation is required.

Key Terms
نذر صوم الأبد (nadhral-ibad): A vow to fast perpetually (every day) as an act of devotion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Breaking a Vow of Perpetual Fasting
Ruling on a person unable to fulfill a vow of perpetual fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who vowed perpetual fasting but cannot continue due to livelihood, and identify the two scenarios (able/unable to pay fidyah).

Core Idea
A vow of perpetual fasting can be broken with fidyah if unable; otherwise seek forgiveness.

This passage addresses a practical dilemma: a person made a vow (nadhr) to fast every day, but later finds it impossible due to the need to earn a living. The Hanafi school provides a clear concession: the vow may be broken, but compensation (fidyah) is required if affordable; otherwise, one seeks Allah's forgiveness. Let us unpack the ruling step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage deals with a vow (nadhr) of perpetual fasting (sawm al-abad). The problem is inability to continue due to preoccupation with earning a livelihood.
The vow is not broken lightly; it's a serious commitment.
2
Extract the primary ruling
The text states: 'he breaks the fast and pays expiation (fidyah).' This is the default ruling when one is unable but can afford fidyah.
Fidyah is typically half a sa' of wheat per missed day.
3
Distinguish the secondary scenario
If the person cannot afford the fidyah due to hardship, then he 'seeks forgiveness from Allah and asks for absolution.' No monetary compensation is required.
This shows the Shari'ah's consideration for genuine incapacity.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling is a concession (rukhsah) based on the maxim that hardship brings ease. A vow does not oblige impossible tasks; compensation or repentance suffices.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on removing hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كمن نذر صوم الابد فضعُف عنه لاشتغاله بالمعيشة يُفطر ويفدى فان لم يقدر على الفدية لعُسرته يستغفر الله تعالى ويستقيله
Like one who vowed perpetual fasting then became weak from it due to preoccupation with livelihood: he breaks the fast and pays expiation. If he cannot afford the expiation due to hardship, he seeks forgiveness from Allah Almighty and asks for absolution.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This is a ruling on a specific situation: a person made a vow (nadhr) to fast every day (perpetual fasting). Later he becomes unable to maintain this due to the need to earn a living. The ruling permits him to break the vow and instead pay fidyah (expiation) for each missed day. The fidyah is half a sa' of wheat per day. If he cannot even afford this fidyah, he should seek Allah's forgiveness and ask for remission of his vow. This is a concession (rukhsah) for those who are genuinely unable to fulfil an arduous vow.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship that is not originally obligatory, made binding by one's own promise.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation for missing a fast, typically half a sa' of wheat per day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) He must perform hajj instead.

Key Takeaway
A perpetual fasting vow can be broken with fidyah if unable; otherwise seek forgiveness.

Expiation for Oath or Killing When Unable to Free a Slave
Ruling on expiation when slave emancipation is impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on fidyah when a person cannot perform primary expiation due to old age or delayed fasting, and explain why fidyah is not permissible.

Core Idea
Once expiation is due, fidyah cannot replace it; fasting is the substitute and must be performed if possible.

This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi principle regarding expiation (kaffara). When expiation is owed for an oath or accidental killing, the primary act is freeing a slave. If unable, one must fast instead. But if one delays fasting until old age, fidyah is not a permissible substitute. This ruling underscores the binding nature of an established obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
Determine that expiation (kaffara) is wajib for breaking an oath or accidental killing.
The primary means is freeing a slave; alternatives are feeding/clothing ten poor for an oath, or fasting two months for killing.
2
Recognize the substitute
If unable to free a slave, fasting becomes the substitute (badal) as per the original ruling.
For oath: fasting three days. For killing: fasting two months consecutively.
3
Understand the condition of old age or delay
If the person is already a shaykh fani (very old) or delayed fasting until becoming senile, they cannot switch to fidyah.
Fidyah is a payment for missed fasts in Ramadan, not for kaffara.
4
Know the alternative
The person should make a will for heirs to free a slave from one-third of the estate if possible; otherwise, they are excused.
This is a recommended (mandoob) or necessary measure to fulfill the obligation if possible.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if someone becomes unable after the obligation is due, they do not pay fidyah but either make a will or, if impossible, the obligation lapses.
This reflects the Hanafi position that established obligations cannot be exchanged for a different form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجبت عليه كفارة يمين او قتل فلم يجد ما يكفّر به من عتق وهو شيخ فان او لم يصم حتى صار فانيا لا يجوز له الفدية لان الصوم هنا بدل عن غيره
And if expiation for an oath or killing becomes obligatory upon him, and he does not find means to expiate by freeing a slave, and he is an old man, or he did not fast until he became senile, then fidyah is not permissible for him because fasting here is a substitute for another (act).
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This ruling addresses a case where expiation (kaffara) is due for breaking an oath or for accidental killing. The primary expiation is freeing a slave. If the person cannot afford to free a slave and he is an old man (shaykh fani) or he had the ability to fast but delayed until he became too old, then he cannot substitute fidyah for the expiation. The reason is that fasting in this context is a substitute (badal) for freeing a slave or feeding the poor, and once an obligation is established, it cannot be exchanged for fidyah later. The recommended action is to make a will for the heirs to free a slave from one-third of the estate. If that is not possible, he is excused.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for a sin or lapse, such as breaking an oath or killing in error.
شيخ فاني (shaykh fani): A very old and decrepit man who is nearing death and unable to perform acts of worship.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation payment, usually for missed fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible because he is unable to fast.
B) It is impermissible because fasting is already a substitute.
C) It is obligatory if he has wealth.
D) It is recommended as an alternative.

Key Takeaway
Fidyah cannot replace an established expiation obligation; if unable to perform the primary or substitute act, a will for freeing a slave is the recommended solution.

Voluntary Fasting: When Can You Break and What Are the Consequences?
Rulings on voluntary fasting with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on breaking a voluntary fast, identify the valid excuse of hospitality, and explain the requirement of qada.

Core Idea
A voluntary fast can be broken with an excuse; once broken, qada is obligatory.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text addresses common situations for a voluntary faster: can you break without a reason? what if you are invited to a meal? must you make up the fast? The answers are provided with clear proofs from the Sunnah and Quran, revealing the balance between leniency and accountability in voluntary worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and list the three distinct rulings: breaking without excuse, hospitality as an excuse, and the obligation of qada upon breaking.
These are the core legal outcomes of the text.
2
Locate the evidence for each ruling
For each ruling, find the specific hadith or verse cited. The first ruling uses the hadith 'al-sa'im al-mutatawwi' amin nafsihi', the second uses the incident with Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, and the third uses Quran 47:33.
Note the chain of transmission for the hadith.
3
Understand the legal implication (wajh al-dalalah)
Analyze how each proof supports the ruling. For example, 'amin nafsihi' indicates the faster has authority over his fast, so breaking is permissible.
This step connects the text to the ruling.
4
Note intra-madhhab variation
Observe that the permissibility without excuse is qualified as 'in one narration' (riwaya), implying a weaker view. The dominant position is that an excuse is preferred.
The text also says 'on the most apparent view' for hospitality, indicating tarjih.
5
Compare cross-madhhab
Consider that the Shafi'i school holds voluntary fasting becomes binding once started and cannot be broken without a shar'i excuse.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for the mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمتطوّع الفطر بلا عذر في رواية والضيافة عذر على الاظهر للضيف والمضيف وله البشارة بهذه الفائدة الجليلة واذا افطر على اى حال عليه القضاء. قال كنت اسمع سماك بن حرب يقول احد بني ام هاني ع . فقال رسول الله الله : الصائم المتطوع أمين نفسه ان شاء صام و ان شاء أفطر ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی افطار الصائم المتطوع ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۷۳۲ ). صنع ابو سعيد الخدرى طعاما فدعا النبي الله و اصحابه فقال رجل من القوم اني صائم فقال له رسول الله الله : صنع لك اخوک و تكلف لك أخوك ، أفطر و صم يو ما مكانه ( دارقطنی ، باب ، ج ثانی ، کتاب الصوم، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۲۲۱۸ رسنن البیھقی ، باب التخيير في القضاء ان كان صومه تطوعا ، ج رابع ص ۴۶۲، نمبر ۸۳۶۲ ). عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله : اذا دعى أحدكم فليجب فان كان مفطرا فليطعم و ان كان صائما فليصل . قال هشام و الصلاة الدعاء ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی الصائم یدعی الی ولیمه ،ص ۳۵۶ نمبر ۲۴۶۰ ). ياايها الذين آمنوا أطيعوا الله و اطيعوا الرسول و لا تبطلوا اعمالكم ( آیت۳۳،سورة محمد ۴۷ ).
It is permissible for the voluntary faster to break without excuse in one narration. Hospitality is an excuse on the most apparent view for the guest and the host, and he has glad tidings through this great benefit. And if he breaks in any case, qada is obligatory upon him. He said: I used to hear Simak ibn Harb say: One of the sons of Umm Hani' said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The voluntary faster is the guardian of his soul; if he wishes he fasts, and if he wishes he breaks.' Abu Sa'id al-Khudri prepared food and invited the Prophet and his Companions. A man from the people said: I am fasting. The Messenger of Allah said to him: 'Your brother has prepared food and put himself out for you; break your fast and fast another day in its place.' From Abu Hurayra: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you is invited, let him respond; if he is not fasting let him eat, and if he is fasting let him pray.' Hisham said: 'Prayer' means supplication. 'O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and do not nullify your deeds.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings on voluntary fasting (sawm al-tatawwu'). First, it is permissible to break a voluntary fast even without any excuse, according to one narration (riwaya), based on the hadith that the voluntary faster is the guardian of his own desire. Second, hospitality (diyafah) is a valid excuse to break the fast, for both the guest and the host, as evidenced by the hadith where the Prophet told a man invited to food to break his fast and fast another day. Third, once the fast is broken, regardless of the reason, making it up (qada) is obligatory, based on the verse 'Do not nullify your deeds' (47:33), which implies that a voluntary act once begun must be completed. The hadith from Abu Hurayra clarifies that a fasting person invited to a meal should respond and supplicate for the host if not eating. These rulings reflect the Hanafi leniency in voluntary worship while maintaining the principle of not wasting acts of obedience.

Key Terms
متطوّع (mutatawwi'): One who performs a voluntary act of worship (nafl).
ضيافة (diyafah): Hospitality; providing food for a guest.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed fast after breaking it voluntarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is allowed without needing qada.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a voluntary faster may break for a valid excuse like hospitality, but must make up the fast (qada).

Ruling on Breaking a Voluntary Fast Without Excuse
States ruling and proof for breaking voluntary fast without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a voluntary fast without excuse and cite the prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
A voluntary faster may break his fast even without excuse, but must make up the day.

When you begin a voluntary fast, you are not bound to complete it under all circumstances. The Hanafi school, relying on authentic hadith, permits breaking a nafl fast even without a legitimate excuse. However, a make-up is required because the act of starting the fast creates a binding obligation. This lesson explores the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon: breaking a voluntary (nafl) fast. Determine the hukm level: in one narration, it is permissible (mubah).
2
Locate the dalil
Locate the prophetic proof: the hadith from Umm Hani' reported in Tirmidhi, where the Prophet said: 'The voluntary faster is master of his own self; if he wishes he may fast, and if he wishes he may break his fast.'
This is a hadith ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves permissibility: the explicit phrase 'if he wishes he may break his fast' gives a choice, indicating that breaking is permitted (ibahah).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that not all Hanafi narrations agree: some early texts prohibit breaking without excuse. The author follows the narration of permissibility as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The difference is within the school, not between schools in this point.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Confirm the operative ruling: it is permissible to break a voluntary fast without excuse, but qada' is necessary because the fast was initiated as a binding obligation (like a nazr).
This is the position adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمتطوّع الفطر بلا عذر في رواية
And it is permissible for the one performing a voluntary fast to break it without an excuse, in one narration.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on voluntary (nafl) fasting. According to one narration, it is permissible for a person who has undertaken a voluntary fast to break it even if there is no legitimate excuse (udhr). This is based on the hadith of Umm Hani' and others, which state that the voluntary faster is 'master of himself'—if he wishes, he may fast, and if he wishes, he may break his fast. The Hanafi school relies on these authentic narrations, though the obligation of qada' (making up) remains, as will be seen later.

Key Terms
متطوّع (mutatawwi‘): A person performing a voluntary (nafl) act of worship, not obligatory.
عذر (‘udhr): A legitimate excuse that permits breaking a fast, such as illness or travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is prohibited and no qada' is required.
B) It is permissible but qada' is required.
C) It is permissible and no qada' is required.
D) It is obligatory to continue the fast.

Key Takeaway
A voluntary faster may break his fast without excuse, but must make up the missed day later.

Hospitality as an Excuse to Break a Voluntary Fast
Ruling with proof: hospitality as an excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hospitality as an excuse to break a voluntary fast, identify the supporting hadith, and explain why it applies to both guest and host.

Core Idea
Hospitality is a valid excuse for both guest and host to break a voluntary fast, based on the Prophet's command.

Fasting is an act of worship, but the Hanafi school recognizes that social bonds and consideration for others can override the merit of a voluntary fast when hospitality is involved. In this short passage, we learn that both the guest and the host may break their nafl fast in order to partake in a meal prepared with effort, and this is confirmed by a clear hadith. Understanding this ruling helps you navigate situations where fasting might inadvertently cause hardship or offense to a host.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is breaking a voluntary (nafl) fast. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) to break it for the reason of hospitality. Note that this is an excuse, not an obligation.
The phrase 'عذر on the most apparent' indicates this is the preferred view among Hanafi scholars.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet commanded a fasting companion to break his fast because the host had prepared food specifically for him.
The hadith is narrated by Darqutni and Bayhaqi, and is considered a hadith ahad with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit command 'أفطر' (break your fast) directly indicates permissibility. The reason given is the host's effort ('تكلف لك أخوك').
The command is understood as permission (ibahah) because it is not an obligation; the hadith also prescribes making up the fast later.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may not consider hospitality a sufficient excuse unless there is genuine hardship. The Hanafi position, however, takes the literal command and extends it to both guest and host.
The author marks this view as 'al-adhhar' (most apparent), indicating it is the relied-upon position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent meaning of the hadith and the principle of removing hardship. This ruling is part of zahir al-riwayah and is mufta bihi.
The glad tidings (bushra) underscore the generosity of the Shariah in such social situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والضيافة عذر على الاظهر للضيف والمضيف وله البشارة بهذه الفائدة الجليلة
And hospitality is an excuse, according to the most apparent view, for both the guest and the host, and glad tidings for him because of this great benefit.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage establishes that hospitality (al-diyafah) constitutes a valid excuse for breaking a voluntary fast. This applies to both the guest (al-dayf) and the host (al-mudif). The evidence comes from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, where the Prophet commanded a fasting companion to break his fast because a host had prepared food specifically for him. The 'most apparent view' (al-adhhar) is that this excuse is valid, and the guest is given glad tidings (bushra) because of this leniency. The Hanafi school thus considers sharing in a meal for hospitality a legitimate reason to break a nafl fast.

Key Terms
ضيافة (diyafah): Hospitality; the act of hosting a guest with food.
ضيف (dayf): Guest; the one who is being hosted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only the host
C) Both the guest and the host
D) Neither the guest nor the host

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits both guest and host to break a voluntary fast when hospitality is involved, based on the Prophet's command to break due to the host's effort.

Obligation to Make Up a Broken Voluntary Fast
States that qada' is required for breaking a voluntary fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada' for a broken voluntary fast and identify the primary evidence from the hadith of 'A'isha that supports it.

Core Idea
Once a voluntary fast is started, it becomes binding and must be made up (qada') if broken.

You may think that voluntary acts are entirely optional, but in Hanafi law, once a voluntary fast is commenced, it takes on the binding force of a vow. This lesson examines the ruling that breaking a voluntary fast requires qada', and the evidence from the Prophet's command to 'A'isha and Hafsa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breaking a voluntary fast. The ruling is that qada' (making it up) is wajib.
This applies regardless of the reason for breaking.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her) where the Prophet ordered her and Hafsa to fast another day after they broke a voluntary fast.
The hadith is narrated in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'sawma makaanahu yawman aakhar' (fast another day in its place) uses a direct imperative (sawma), which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
This command is taken as proof that qada' is fard/wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Hanbali) do not require qada' for a broken voluntary fast, viewing the hadith as non-binding or specific to that incident. Hanafi and Shafi'i hold qada' is wajib.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the clear command of the Prophet and the principle that a commenced voluntary act becomes analogous to a vow (nazr), which must be fulfilled.
This ruling is consistent with zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا افطر على اى حال عليه القضاء
And if he breaks his fast in any case, he must make up for it.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This ruling establishes that whenever a voluntary fast is broken, regardless of the reason or excuse, the person is obligated to perform qada'—that is, fast another day in its place. The author supports this with multiple proofs: (1) The Qur'anic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33) implies that once started, the fast should not be invalidated without compensation. (2) Once a voluntary act is commenced, it becomes like a voluntary vow (nazr) and is binding to complete. (3) A hadith from 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her) reports that the Prophet ordered her and Hafsa to fast another day when they broke their voluntary fast. (4) The saying of the tabi'in Hasan and Ibrahim: 'If someone intends to fast at night and then breaks it, qada' is required.' Thus, qada' is wajib (obligatory) even if the break was with a valid excuse.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): The act of fulfilling an obligation after its prescribed time; here, fasting a day in place of a broken voluntary fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required when a voluntary fast is broken?
A) Only repentance (tawbah)
B) Nothing, because it was voluntary
C) Making up the fast (qada')
D) Feeding a poor person

Key Takeaway
Once a voluntary fast is commenced, it becomes binding; breaking it necessitates qada' (making it up) as wajib.

No Qada for Voluntary Fast on Prohibited Days
Ruling on voluntary fasts on five prohibited days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no qada is required for a voluntary fast on prohibited days and explain the proof from the hadith prohibition.

Core Idea
A voluntary fast on a prohibited day is invalid from the start — no qada required.

This lesson addresses a specific exception to the general rule that a voluntary fast, once started, must be either completed or made up if broken. The exception concerns the five days on which fasting is prohibited: the two Eids and the three days of Tashriq. Unlike ordinary days, a fast begun on these days does not take effect at all, so breaking it imposes no duty of qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is starting a voluntary fast on any of the five prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three days of Tashriq). The ruling is that if the fast is broken, no qada is required.
This is an exception to the general rule that voluntary fasts require qada if broken.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the explicit prohibition of fasting on these days from authentic hadith. The passage alludes to the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab reporting the Prophet's prohibition of fasting on the two Eids.
The hadith is sahih, giving it qati' thubut (certain transmission).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (nahy) indicates that the act of fasting on these days is not valid as worship. Since the fast never becomes valid ('in'iqad), breaking it does not create an obligation of qada.
Hanafi usul: nahy indicates fasād (invalidity) of the commanded act if intended as worship.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that a voluntary fast on a prohibited day is valid but sinful, so qada is required if broken. Their proof is that the prohibition relates to the reward, not the validity.
This difference stems from differing usul on the effect of nahy on ibadat.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi within the school, supported by the explicit hadith and the principle that a prohibited act cannot be a valid act of worship.
Al-Marghinani and other Hanafi authorities affirm this as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في عوارض الصوم
الا اذا شرع متطوعا في خمسة ايام يومى العيدين وايام التشريق فلا يلزمه قضائها بافسادها في ظاهر الرواية . والله اعلم.
Section on obstacles to fasting. Except if one begins a voluntary fast on the five days: the two Eids and the days of Tashriq, then it is not necessary for him to make them up if he spoils them in the apparent narration. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if a person voluntarily (mutatawwi') starts a fast on one of the five days that are prohibited for fasting according to the Shari'ah - namely, the two 'Eids (al-Fitr and al-Adha) and the three days after 'Eid al-Adha called Ayyam al-Tashriq - then if he breaks that fast, he is not obliged to make it up (qada) according to the zahir al-riwayah (the well-known transmission within the Hanafi school). The reason is that these days are not valid for fasting at all; the fast does not take effect ('in'iqad) because the Shari'ah prohibits fasting on them. Since the fast is not valid, there is no qada. The passage then mentions that Abu Hanifa's ruling is that the fast is not concluded (mun'aqid) on these days. The author provides two proofs: (1) requiring qada would imply affirming fasting on these days, which is prohibited; (2) authentic hadith from Umar ibn al-Khattab and from Nabisha al-Hudhali state that the Messenger of Allah forbade fasting on the two 'Eids and said the days of Tashriq are days of eating and drinking. Thus, the ruling is specific to the Hanafi school's principle that a prohibited act cannot be validly begun as worship.

Key Terms
عوارض الصوم ('awarid al-sawm): Obstacles or exceptional circumstances that affect the ruling of fasting, such as prohibited days.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school, especially from Imam Muhammad's six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone starts a voluntary fast on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr and then breaks it, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must make up the fast later.
B) He does not need to make it up because the day is prohibited for fasting.
C) He must pay kaffarah for breaking a voluntary fast.
D) The fast is valid and he must complete it.

Key Takeaway
A voluntary fast started on a day when fasting is prohibited (Eidain and Ayyam al-Tashriq) is invalid from the outset, and breaking it does not require qada.

Vowing Fasts on Eid and Tashriq Days
Ruling on vowing fasts on Eid and Tashriq days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vowing fasts on prohibited days and apply it by identifying the required action (break and make up).

Core Idea
A vow on a prohibited day is valid but must be fulfilled on another day.

We often think a vow to fast on a forbidden day is invalid, but the Hanafi school rules otherwise. This lesson examines the preferred view (al-mukhtar) that such a vow is valid, yet the fast must be broken on the prohibited day and made up later. The evidence from hadith and the logic behind this ruling will be clarified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Vowing to fast on Eid or Tashriq days. The ruling is that the vow is valid (sahih), but the fast on the prohibited day is forbidden (haram).
The act is a nadhr (vow) of sawm on days when sawm is prohibited.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: one forbidding fasting on Eid days, and another showing that a vow coinciding with Eid is valid but must be made up.
The first hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim; the second is from Ibn Umar in Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (nahy) from the first hadith makes fasting on the day haram, but the second hadith shows that the vow itself is not invalidated because the prohibition is about performing the fast, not about the vow.
The vow is an independent act; its validity depends on its own conditions, not on the day.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers such a vow invalid because the vowed act is inherently sinful on that day. The Hanafi school holds the vow valid because the intent is obedience, and the prohibition is overridden by the need to fulfill the vow on another day.
Intra-Hanafi: some earlier Hanafi scholars also considered the vow invalid, but al-mukhtar (preferred) is validity.
5
Apply the ruling
The mufta bihi (operative position) is: the vow is valid, the person must not fast on the prohibited day, must break if started, and must make up the fast on another day. If he does fast on the prohibited day, it counts as valid but with karahah.
This harmonizes the obligation of fulfilling vows with the prohibition of fasting on those days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۷)، اور مختار مذہب میں عید اور ایام تشریق میں روزے کی منت ماننا صحیح ہے، اور ان ایام میں روزہ ) کو توڑنا اور اس کی قضا کرنا واجب ہے، اور اگر کسی نے ان دنوں میں منت کے روزے رکھ ہی لئے تو کراہت تحریمی کے ساتھ کافی ہو سکتے ہیں۔ تشریح : ان پانچ دنوں میں روزہ رکھنا ممنوع ہے اس لئے ان دنوں میں روزہ رکھنے کی منت نہیں ماننی چاہئے لیکن اگر کسی نے مان لی تو نذر ہو جائے گی ، اس لئے ان دنوں میں روزہ نہ رکھے ، اور بعد میں انکی قضا کرے ، مناسب یہی ہے لیکن اگر کسی نے ان دنوں میں روزہ رکھ ہی لیا تو نذر کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ ناقص نذر مانی تھی اس لئے ناقص ہی ادا کر دی گئی ۔ وجه : (1) اس دن اس لئے روزہ نہ رکھے کہ حضور نے اس دن روزہ رکھنے سے منع فرمایا ہے کہ اس دن اللہ تعالی کے یہاں دعوت ہوتی ہے، حدیث یہ ہے۔ شهدت العيد مع عمر بن الخطاب فقال هذان يومان نهى رسول الله الا الله . صيامهما يوم فطركم من صيامكم واليوم الآخر تأكلون فيه من نسككم - بخاری شریف ، باب صوم یوم الفطر ، ص ۳۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۹۰ر مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم صوم یومی العیدین ، ص ۴۶۴، نمبر ۲۶۷۱/۱۱۳۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عید کے دن اور بقر عید کے دن روزہ نہیں رکھنا چاہئے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نذر تو ہو جائے گی لیکن بعد میں اس کی قضاء کرے، حدیث یہ ہے۔ جاء رجل الى ابن عمر فقال رجل نذر أن يصوم يوما قال اظنه قال الاثنين فوافق ذالک یوم عید فقال ابن عمر أمر الله بوفاء النذر و نهى النبي الا الله له عن صوم هذا اليوم . Translation (127): In the preferred view, vowing to fast on Eid and the days of Tashriq is valid, and it is obligatory to break the fast on those days and make them up later. But if someone does fast on those days, it is valid with tanzihan makruh. Elaboration: Fasting on these five days is prohibited, so one should not vow to fast on them. But if someone did make such a vow, the vow becomes valid. So he should not fast on those days and should make them up later. That is proper. But if he does fast on them, the vowed fast is fulfilled, because he made a deficient vow and fulfilled it deficiently. Evidence: (1) The Prophet forbade fasting on these days; hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. (2) Another hadith shows that the vow is valid but must be made up.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on vowing to fast on the prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three days of Tashriq). According to the preferred opinion in the Hanafi school (al-mukhtar), such a vow is valid despite the prohibition. The person must not fast on those days; instead, he must break the fast (if he begins) and make it up later. If he does fast on the prohibited day, the fast counts for the vow but he incurs sin (makruh tahrimi). The proof includes hadith from Bukhari and Muslim forbidding fasting on Eid days, and a hadith from Ibn Umar showing that a vow coinciding with Eid must be fulfilled by making it up.

Key Terms
ایام تشریق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
مختار (mukhtar): The preferred opinion within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Not fast on Eid and make up later.
C) The vow is invalid, so nothing required.
D) Fast on Eid and pay kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
A vow to fast on a prohibited day is valid in the Hanafi school; the fast must be broken on that day and made up later.

The Obligation of Fulfilling a Vow
States the general principle of vow fulfillment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for unconditional and conditional vows and identify when fulfillment becomes wajib.

Core Idea
A vow becomes binding once its condition is met or immediately if unconditional.

In this passage, we learn the foundational ruling of vow fulfillment. Whether the vow is unconditional (mutlaq) or conditional upon a future event (mu'allaq bi shart), the moment the condition occurs, the vow must be fulfilled. This principle governs all vows in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of vow
Determine whether the vow is unconditional (mutlaq) or conditional (mu'allaq bi shart). The text explicitly mentions both categories.
2
Check if the condition has occurred
For a conditional vow, fulfillment is only required once the condition takes place. For an unconditional vow, fulfillment is immediate.
If the condition never occurs, the vow does not become binding.
3
State the ruling
Once the condition is met (or vow is unconditional), fulfillment becomes wajib (obligatory). The text uses 'lazimahu al-wafa' bihi'.
This is a general rule, not specific to fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he makes a vow unconditionally or conditionally upon a condition and it occurs, fulfillment is incumbent upon him. (1127) And the vow of fasting on the two 'Eids and the days of Tashriq is valid in the chosen position, and it is obligatory to break them and make them up, and if he fasts them, it suffices with Karahah. (1128) Translation: (127): And in the chosen madhhab, vowing to fast on 'Eid and the days of Tashriq is valid, and breaking the fast on those days and making them up is obligatory, and if someone fasts them for a vow, it is sufficient with Tahrimi Karahah. Explanation: Fasting on these five days is prohibited, so one should not vow to fast on them, but if someone does vow, the vow is valid, so he should not fast on those days and should make them up later; that is appropriate. But if he fasts them, the vow is fulfilled because he made a defective vow so he fulfilled it defectively. Evidence: (1) He should not fast on that day because the Prophet ﷺ prohibited fasting on it, as that day is a feast with Allah. Hadith: I witnessed 'Eid with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, and he said: These are two days that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ prohibited fasting: the day of your breaking fast from your fasting, and the other day on which you eat from your sacrifices. (Bukhari, Bab Sawm Yawm al-Fitr, p. 320, no. 1990; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Sawm Yawmay al-'Eidayn, p. 464, no. 2671/1137) This hadith indicates that one should not fast on 'Eid and the Day of Sacrifice. (2) This hadith states that the vow is valid but must be made up later. A man came to Ibn 'Umar and said: A man vowed to fast a day, and it coincided with 'Eid. Ibn 'Umar said: Allah commands fulfillment of vows, and the Prophet ﷺ prohibited fasting on this day. (Bukhari, Bab Sawm Yawm al-Nahr, p. 320, no. 1993)
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the chapter on vows. First, a vow (nadhr) may be unconditional (mutlaq) or conditional (mu'allaq bi shart). Once the condition occurs, fulfillment becomes necessary. This is a general principle. Second, the text addresses the specific case of vowing to fast on the two 'Eids and the days of Tashriq (the three days after 'Eid al-Adha). In the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar), such a vow is valid (sahih). However, since fasting on these days is prohibited, the person must break the fast (yajibu fatruha) and later make it up (qada'). If one does fast, the vow is technically fulfilled (yujzi'uhu), but with karahah tahrimiyah (prohibitively disliked). The 'illah (reason) is that the vow itself is valid, but the time is prohibited; hence the fulfillment is imperfect. The evidence from hadith clearly prohibits fasting on these days, yet another hadith shows that a vow coinciding with 'Eid must still be fulfilled by making it up later. Thus, the Hanafi position balances the prohibition and the obligation of vow fulfillment.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow, a pledge to perform an act of worship (or similar) if a condition is met or unconditionally.
مطلق (mutlaq): Unconditional; a vow not tied to any condition.
معلّق بشرط (mu'allaq bi shart): Conditional upon something; the vow takes effect only when the condition occurs.

Vowing to Fast on Prohibited Days
States the ruling on vowing to fast on prohibited days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on vowing to fast on Eid and Tashriq days, explain the obligation to break and make up, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
Vowing to fast on prohibited days is valid but requires breaking the fast and making it up.

This passage addresses a specific and commonly misunderstood scenario: a person vows to fast on Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, or the days of Tashriq. While these days are clearly prohibited for fasting, the Hanafi school holds that the vow itself is valid. However, the person must not keep the fast on those days; instead, they must break it and make up the fast later. If they do fast, it technically fulfills the vow but with karahah tahrimiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prohibition
First, note that fasting on the two Eids and the three days of Tashriq is haram (prohibited) based on clear hadith. The text provides the hadith of Umar.
2
State the validity of the vow
Despite the prohibition, the Hanafi mukhtar (chosen) position is that such a vow is valid (sahih). This is because the vow itself is an act of devotion; the flaw is in the timing, not the act.
Some schools consider the vow invalid.
3
Identify the obligation
Since the day is prohibited, the one who made the vow must break the fast on that day and make it up later. This is wajib.
Breaking the fast is obligatory, not optional.
4
Consider the scenario if he fasts
If the person ignores the prohibition and fasts, the fast is still valid for fulfilling the vow, but it is accompanied by karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked).
The act remains sinful due to fasting on a prohibited day.
5
Note the evidence
The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Allah commands fulfillment of vows, and the Prophet prohibited fasting on this day.' This combines the obligation of vow with the prohibition, leading to the ruling of make-up.

12 min
Ignoring Specification and Conditional Timing in Vows
Explains that specification of time/place/dirham/faqir is ignored in vows; substitution valid; conditional vows require condition first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that specification in vows is non-binding and explain the requirement of condition fulfillment for conditional vows, applying these to given scenarios.

Core Idea
In Hanafi vows, the essential act suffices; accidental specifications like time/place/recipient are ignored, and a conditional vow only becomes binding after the condition occurs.

This passage from the fiqh of nadhr (vows) clarifies two key principles: the flexibility in fulfilling a vow despite specifications, and the strict sequence for conditional vows. The Hanafi school relies on prophetic practice and companion sayings to support these rulings, emphasizing the intention over incidental details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
Vows (nadhr) are wajib to fulfill. Understand that the essence of the vow is the act itself, not its accidental specifications.
General principle: the vow attaches to the act, not its attributes.
2
Analyze the first ruling: ignoring specification
The text lists four specifications: time (e.g., Sha'ban), place (Makkah), dirham (specific coin), and poor person (specific faqir). The Hanafi position is that these are not binding; substitution with an equivalent act suffices.
The ruling applies unless the specification is made a condition (shart) in the vow's phrasing.
3
Examine the dalil for specification ruling
The passage cites a mursal hadith where the Prophet ﷺ allowed a man who vowed to pray in Bayt al-Maqdis to pray in Makkah instead, and the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab allowing substitution of mosques for i'tikaf.
These proofs show that the specified place is not essential; the intent of worship suffices.
4
Distinguish the second ruling: conditional vows
If a vow is suspended on a condition (mu'allaq), e.g., 'If my son recovers, I will fast two days,' the vow becomes wajib only after the condition occurs. Performing the act before the condition is invalid.
Analogy to oaths: the consequence must follow the condition, not precede it.
5
Apply the sequence
Practice: Given a conditional vow, identify the condition and the act. The act must be performed after the condition is fulfilled, not before.
If performed before, the vow remains unfulfilled and must be repeated after the condition.

(مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب النذ ربا مشی الی بیت المقدس، ج ثامن بی ۱۳۹۵، نمبر ۱۶۱۶۹) ترجمه : (۱۲۹) اگرمنت کو کسی شرط کے ساتھ معلق کیا تو شرط کے پائے جانے سے پہلے منت کو پورا کرنا کافی نہیں۔ (شرط پوری ہونے کے بعد منت پوری کرنی ہو گی )۔ تشریح : نذر کو کسی شرط پر معلق کیا ، مثلا نذرمانی کہ بیٹا تندرست ہو گا دو روزے رکھوں گا، ابھی تندرست بھی نہیں ہوا تھا کہ دو روزے رکھ لئے تو یہ کافی نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ تندرست ہونے کے بعد اس پر روزے واجب ہوں گے اور دوبارہ دوروزے رکھنا ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ حانث پہلے ہوا ہو اور کفارہ بعد میں ادا کرے۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال قال رسول الله من حلف عـلـى يـمـيـن فراى غيرها خيرا منها فليأت الذي هو خير وليكفر عن يمينه - (مسلم شریف، باب ندب من حلف یمینا فرای غیر ها خیر امنها ان یاتی الذی هو خیر و یکفر عن یمینه ، ص ۷۲۵ نمبر ۴۲۷۳/۱۶۵۰ / بخاری شریف، باب قول اللہ تعالی لا
We disregard the specification of time, place, dirham, and poor person. So fasting in Rajab suffices for his vow to fast in Sha'ban, and praying two rak'ahs in Egypt for his vow to pray them in Makkah, and giving charity with any dirham for the specific dirham, and spending on Zayd (the poor person) for his vow to spend on 'Amr. (1128) And if he suspends the vow upon a condition, what he did before the existence of that condition does not suffice for him. (1129) Translation: (128) We regard the specification of time, place, dirham, and poor person as invalid. So if he vows to fast in Sha'ban, fasting in Rajab suffices. If he vows to pray two rak'ahs in Makkah, praying in Egypt suffices. If he vows to give a specific dirham, giving any dirham suffices. If he vows to spend on Zayd (a poor person), spending on 'Amr suffices. Explanation: Four examples: [1] If he specifies a time, it is better to do it at that time, but if he does it at another time, the vow is still fulfilled. [2] If he specifies a place, praying elsewhere suffices. [3] If he specifies a dirham, another dirham suffices. [4] If he specifies a poor person, giving to another suffices. Evidence: (1) This mursal hadith shows that fulfilling at a specific place is not necessary. (Hadith from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah: ...) (2) The saying of a companion: Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab said that if one vows i'tikaf in Masjid Ilya', i'tikaf in Masjid al-Nabawi suffices. Translation: (129) If the vow is suspended on a condition, fulfilling it before the condition occurs is not sufficient. (It must be fulfilled after the condition is met.) Explanation: If he vows, 'If my son recovers, I will fast two days,' and he fasts before recovery, it does not suffice; he must fast after recovery. Evidence: (1) Hadith: 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better, let him do that which is better and expiate his oath.' (Muslim and Bukhari)
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings from the chapter on vows. The first ruling (1128) establishes that in a vow, any specification of time, place, amount (dirham), or recipient (faqir) is effectively ignored (mulgha). This means the vow is fulfilled by doing an equivalent act at a different time, place, with a different dirham, or for a different poor person. The Hanafi school bases this on the principle that the essence of the vow is the act itself, not its accidental attributes (unless specified as an essential condition). The evidence includes a mursal hadith where the Prophet ﷺ allowed a man who vowed to pray in Bayt al-Maqdis to pray in Makkah instead, and the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab allowing substitution of a mosque for i'tikaf. The second ruling (1129) deals with conditional vows (mu'allaq). If a vow is conditioned on something, performing the vowed act before the condition occurs is invalid; the condition must be met first. This is analogous to an oath (yamin): one should not fulfill the consequence before the condition. The proof is a hadith about oaths: if one swears and finds something better, he should do the better thing and expiate, implying the sequence. Thus, in a conditional vow, the fulfillment is only valid after the condition.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yeen): Specification; designating a particular time, place, dirham, or person in a vow.
معلق (mu'allaq): Conditional; a vow suspended on a future event.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or broken vow or act of worship.
فقیر (faqir): A poor person eligible to receive charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, if a person vows, 'I will fast in Rajab' but fasts in Sha'ban with the intention of that vow, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The vow is not fulfilled because he changed the month.
B) The vow is fulfilled because specification of time is ignored.
C) He must fast again in Rajab to fulfill the vow.
D) He must expiate for breaking the vow.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, vows are fulfilled by the essential act; accidental specifications like time, place, amount, and recipient are ignored, and conditional vows require the condition to be met first.

Definition and Conditions of I'tikaf
Defines i'tikaf and states its validity conditions including mosque with congregation and ruling for women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of i'tikaf, list its four components, and identify the conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is valid only in a mosque with five daily congregations for men, and in a home prayer space for women.

This passage defines i'tikaf and lays out the conditions that make it valid. You will learn that i'tikaf is not simply staying in any mosque—it requires a specific type of mosque with regular congregational prayers, and for women, an exception is made. Understanding these conditions is essential to perform this sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four components of i'tikaf
From the text, list the four essential elements: staying (iqāmah), being in a mosque, intention (niyyah), and fasting (sawm). All four must be present for i'tikaf to be valid.
The text states 'the name i'tikaf is given to a combination of four things'.
2
Determine the required type of mosque for men
The text states that i'tikaf must be in a mosque where the five daily prayers are actually performed in congregation. The chosen (mukhtār) view requires that the congregation be established for all five prayers.
The mosque must have an imam and mu'adhdhin, indicating regular congregation.
3
State the ruling for women
For a woman, i'tikaf is valid in the 'mosque of her house'—the place she has designated for prayer. This is an exception based on the need for hijab.
The text says 'for a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house'.
4
Identify the primary proofs (dalil)
The Quranic verse (2:187) mentions i'tikaf in mosques, and hadith from Aisha and Hudhayfa specify that i'tikaf must be in a congregational mosque (masjid jāmi').
The hadith are cited in the commentary: Abu Dawud and Dar Qutni.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a man who wants to perform i'tikaf in a mosque that only holds Friday prayers. According to the Hanafi chosen view, his i'tikaf would be invalid because daily congregation is missing.
This illustrates the practical implication of the condition.

باب الاعتكاف (۱۱۳۰) هو الاقامة بنيته في مسجد تقام فيه الجماعة بالفعل للصلوات الخمس فلا يصح في مسجد لا تقام فيه الجماعة للصلوة على المختار . (۱۱۳۱) وللمرأة الاعتكاف في مسجد بيتها ضروری نوٹ : الاعتكاف : علف سے مشتق ہے کسی جگہ شہر نا اور لازم پکڑنا مسجد میں روزے کے ساتھ ٹھہرنے کو یہاں اعتکاف کہا ہے ۔ چار باتوں کے مجموعے کا نام اعتکاف ہے [1] شہر نا[۲] مسجد ہونا [۳] اعتکاف کی نیت ہو [۴] روزہ ہو۔ اعتکاف کرنے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ولا تباشروهن وانتم عاكفون في المساجد تلك حدود الله فلا تقربوها . (آیت ۱۸۷ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں اعتکاف کرنے کی دلیل ہے۔ اعتکاف سنت ہے اس کی دلیل آگے آرہی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۰) اعتکاف کی نیت سے ایسی مسجد میں قیام کرنا جس میں اس وقت پانچوں نمازوں کی جماعت ہوتی ہوں اعتکاف ہے۔ پس مختار مذہب میں ایسی مسجد میں اعتکاف ) صحیح نہیں جس میں نماز کی جماعت نہ ہوتی ہو۔ تشریح : یہ اعتکاف کی تعریف ہے، کہ جس مسجد میں پانچوں وقتوں کی جماعت ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف کی نیت سے ٹھہرنے کو اعتکاف، کہتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ جس مسجد میں اس وقت جماعت سے نماز نہ ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة انها قالت السنة على المعتكف ان لا يعود مريضا ولا يشهد جنازة ولا يمس امرأة ولا يباشرها ولا يخرج لحاجة الا لما لا بد منه ولا اعتكاف الا بصوم ولا اعتكاف الا في مسجد جامع (ابو داؤد شریف، المعتلف یعود المریض ص ۱۳۴۲ نمبر ۲۴۷۳ / دار قطنی ، باب الاعتکاف ج ثانی ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۲۳۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے صلى الله عليه وسلم کہ جماعت والی مسجد میں اعتکاف ہوگا۔ (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن حذيفة قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول كل مسجد له مؤذن وامام فالاعتكاف فيه يصلح (دار قطنی ، باب الاعتكاف، ج ثانی ص ۱۷۹، نمبر ۲۳۲۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسی مسجد میں جس میں پنج وقتہ نماز ہوتی ہو اس میں اعتکاف جائز ہے (۳) چونکہ جماعت کے ساتھ مختلف کونماز پڑھنی ہوگی اس لئے جس مسجد میں پنج وقتہ نماز نہ ہوتی ہو وہاں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے میں دقت ہوگی ۔ ترجمہ : (۱۱۳۱) اور عورت کا اعتکاف اپنے گھر کی مسجد میں ہے، اور ( گھر کی مسجد ) وہ جگہ ہے جس کو نماز کے لئے معین کر لیا ہو
Chapter of I'tikaf (1130) I'tikaf is staying with intention in a mosque in which the congregation for the five prayers is actually established. So it is not valid in a mosque in which the congregation for prayer is not established, according to the chosen view. (1131) For a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house. Necessary note: I'tikaf is derived from 'akafa, meaning to stay and stick to a place. Here it refers to staying in a mosque with fasting. The name i'tikaf is given to a combination of four things: [1] Staying, [2] Being in a mosque, [3] Having the intention of i'tikaf, [4] Fasting. The proof for performing i'tikaf is this verse: 'And do not have relations with them while you are in i'tikaf in the mosques. These are the limits of Allah, so do not approach them.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187) This verse provides evidence for i'tikaf. I'tikaf is sunnah; its evidence will come later. Translation: (130) I'tikaf is staying with the intention of i'tikaf in a mosque in which the five prayers are performed in congregation at that time. So according to the chosen madhhab, i'tikaf is not valid in a mosque in which prayer with congregation is not held. Explanation: This is the definition of i'tikaf: staying in a mosque where the five daily prayers are performed in congregation, with the intention of i'tikaf, is called i'tikaf. Therefore, i'tikaf in a mosque where prayer with congregation is not performed at that time is not valid. Proof: (1) From 'Aisha that she said: 'The sunnah for the person in i'tikaf is that he does not visit the sick, does not attend a funeral, does not touch a woman nor have relations with her, and does not go out for any need except what is unavoidable, and there is no i'tikaf except with fasting, and there is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the person in i'tikaf visiting the sick, p. 1342, no. 2473; Dar Qutni, chapter on i'tikaf, vol. 2, p. 181, no. 2339) This hadith indicates that i'tikaf is in a congregational mosque. (2) Another hadith: From Hudhayfa that he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Every mosque that has a mu'adhdhin and an imam, i'tikaf in it is valid.' (Dar Qutni, chapter on i'tikaf, vol. 2, p. 179, no. 23232) This hadith shows that i'tikaf is permissible in a mosque where the five daily prayers are performed. (3) Because one must pray the different prayers with congregation, it would be difficult to pray with congregation in a mosque where the five daily prayers are not performed. Translation: (1131) For a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house, and the 'mosque of her house' is a place she has designated for prayer.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage provides the definition and conditions of i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school. The matn (ruling 1130) defines i'tikaf as staying (iqāmah) with intention (niyyah) in a mosque where the five daily prayers are actually performed in congregation. The phrase 'al-mukhtār' (the chosen view) indicates this is the relied-upon position. The text then adds (ruling 1131) that for a woman, i'tikaf is valid in the 'mosque of her house', i.e., the place she has designated for prayer. The commentary explains the linguistic derivation and lists four necessary components: staying, mosque, intention, and fasting. The proof is from the Quran (2:187) which mentions i'tikaf in mosques, and from hadith of 'Aisha and Hudhayfa which specify that i'tikaf must be in a congregational mosque (masjid jāmi'). The reasoning (wajh) adds a rational point: since one must pray the five prayers in congregation, it would be difficult in a mosque without congregation, so the condition ensures the ability to fulfill that sunnah. For women, they cannot go to the public mosque for i'tikaf if they observe proper hijab, so their i'tikaf is valid at home.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Staying in a mosque with the intention of worship, accompanied by fasting, for a specific period.
مسجد (masjid): A physical structure designated for prayer; for men, a public mosque; for women, a designated prayer space in the home.
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed with at least two people (including the imam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi chosen view in this text, in which of the following places is a man's i'tikaf valid?
A) In a mosque where only Friday prayers are held, but no daily congregational prayers.
B) In a neighborhood mosque where the five daily prayers are performed in congregation.
C) In his own house in a prayer room.
D) In an open field designated for Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf requires a mosque with five daily congregations for men, and a designated home prayer space for women, along with intention and fasting.

Fasting as a Condition for Vowed I'tikaaf
States that fasting is a condition for validity of vowed i'tikaaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that fasting is a condition (shart) for the validity of a vowed i'tikaaf, and explain the proof from the two cited hadith.

Core Idea
Fasting is a condition for vowed i'tikaaf only, not for sunnah or mustahabb i'tikaaf.

This lesson clarifies a specific fiqh rule: when a person vows to perform i'tikaaf, fasting becomes obligatory as a condition (shart) for its validity. The Hanafi school bases this on explicit prophetic commands. The passage presents two hadith as evidence, and distinguishes between vowed and non-vowed i'tikaaf. Understanding this distinction is important to avoid a common misunderstanding that fasting is required for all types of i'tikaaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the Arabic matn: والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور. Note that it specifies 'al-mandhoor' (the vowed). This limits the condition to vowed i'tikaaf only.
The Urdu translation reinforces: صرف منت کے روزے کے لئے روزہ شرط ہے.
2
Examine the first hadith
The hadith from Aisha states: لا اعتكاف الا بصيام (No i'tikaaf except with fasting). Consider how Hanafis interpret this general statement as applying specifically to vowed i'tikaaf based on context and other evidence.
This hadith is reported by al-Daraqutni. Its chain is ahad, so it gives zanni thubut.
3
Examine the second hadith
The hadith from Ibn Umar: When Umar vowed to perform i'tikaaf, the Prophet instructed him: اعتكف و صم (Perform i'tikaaf and fast). This directly links fasting with vowed i'tikaaf.
This hadith is also ahad, but the command is explicit.
4
Recognize the Hanafi principle
In Hanafi fiqh, fasting is a shart (condition) for the validity of vowed i'tikaaf. Omitting fasting invalidates the i'tikaaf. This is distinct from a rukn (pillar) — the act is invalid, not just deficient.
For non-vowed i'tikaaf, fasting is recommended but not required.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that fasting is not a condition for vowed i'tikaaf. He interprets the hadith differently or considers them weak. The Hanafi position relies on these hadith as sufficient evidence.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Shafi'i school, one can perform a vowed i'tikaaf without fasting and it is valid.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصوم شرط لصحة المنذور
ترجمه : (۱۱۳۳) صرف منت کے روزے کے لئے روزہ شرط ہے۔
تشریح : اگر نذرمانی کہ ایک دن کا اعتکاف کروں گا تو نذر کے اعتکاف کے ساتھ روزہ رکھنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة ان النبي عل الله قال لا اعتكاف الا بصيام (دارقطنی ، باب الاعتکاف ج ثانی ص ۷۹ نمبر ۲۳۳۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روزے کے بغیر اعتکاف نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے، عـن ابـن عـمـر أن عمر قال اللهم انى نذرت أن أعتكف يو ما قال : اعتكف و صم (دار قطنی ، باب الاعتکاف ج ثانی ص۱۸۰ نمبر ۲۳۳۶ سنن بیہقی ، باب المختلف يصوم، ج رابع ، ص ۵۲۰، نمبر ۸۵۷۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اعتکاف کی نذر مانی تو فرمایا کہ اعتکاف کرو اور روزہ بھی رکھو۔
And fasting is a condition for the validity of the vowed [i'tikaaf]. Translation (1133): Fasting is necessary only for the vowed fast. Explanation: If one vows to perform i'tikaaf for one day, then fasting alongside the vowed i'tikaaf is also necessary. Evidence: (1) From Aisha that the Prophet said: No i'tikaaf except with fasting. (2) This hadith: From Ibn Umar that Umar said: O Allah, I have vowed to perform i'tikaaf for a day. He said: Perform i'tikaaf and fast.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof clarifying that fasting is a condition for the validity of a vowed i'tikaaf. The Arabic matn states: 'Fasting is a condition for the validity of the vowed.' The Urdu translation specifies that fasting is required only for the vowed i'tikaaf, not for other types. The explanation elaborates: if one vows to perform i'tikaaf for one day, fasting becomes necessary alongside it. Two hadith are cited as proof. The first is from Aisha: 'No i'tikaaf except with fasting' (reported by al-Daraqutni). The second is from Ibn Umar that when Umar vowed to perform i'tikaaf, the Prophet instructed him to both perform i'tikaaf and fast. In the Hanafi school, this condition applies specifically to the vowed i'tikaaf (al-mandhoor). For non-vowed i'tikaaf (sunnah or mustahabb), fasting is not a condition. This is based on the principle that a vow adds obligation beyond the original ruling.

Key Terms
المنذور (al-mandhoor): The vowed i'tikaaf, which becomes obligatory by the vow.
شرط الصحة (shart al-sihhah): A condition for the validity of the act; without it the i'tikaaf is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of i'tikaaf is fasting a condition?
A) All types of i'tikaaf.
B) The sunnah mu'akkadah during Ramadan.
C) The vowed (nadhr) i'tikaaf only.
D) The mustahabb i'tikaaf.

Key Takeaway
For vowed i'tikaaf, fasting is a necessary condition (shart) for validity; without fasting, the i'tikaaf is invalid.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Exiting the Mosque During I'tikaf
Explains rulings on permissible and impermissible exits from i'tikaf with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible exits from i'tikaf, apply the Hanafi rule on invalidating exits, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Exiting i'tikaf without a genuine need breaks the required continuity, even for an hour.

Not every exit from the mosque during i'tikaf is forbidden. The tradition recognizes religious, natural, and emergency exemptions. However, any needless departure—even a short one—voids the i'tikaf according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, whereas the Sahibayn require half a day of absence. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify permissible exit categories
Read the passage and list the three types of exits that are allowed: religious needs (like Friday prayer), natural needs (like urination), and emergency necessities (like mosque collapse, coercion, danger to life/property).
For emergencies, the mu'takif must immediately proceed to another mosque; any other activity invalidates i'tikaf.
2
State the general rule for impermissible exits
The passage states: any exit without excuse, even for an hour, invalidates wajib i'tikaf and terminates sunnah i'tikaf. Notice the terms 'fasad' (invalid) for wajib and 'intaha' (ends) for other types.
Wajib i'tikaf (e.g., vowed) must be restarted from the beginning. Sunnah i'tikaf (e.g., last ten days) loses continuity; past days count but the remaining period becomes separate if resumed.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any needless exit invalidates. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only if the exit is for half a day or more. This disagreement is recorded in al-Hidayah.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) is Imam Abu Hanifa's view due to caution and stronger textual support.
4
Apply to wajib vs sunnah i'tikaf
For wajib (vowed) i'tikaf, an invalid exit requires a complete restart. For sunnah i'tikaf, the current i'tikaf ends, but the days already performed count. Resumption starts a new i'tikaf.
Example: Vowed 10 days, exit on day 5 → invalid, restart 10 days. Sunnah last ten days, exit on day 6 → 6 days count, remaining 4 become new i'tikaf if continued.
